- Easier than past tense conjugations
- Ultra-granular approach: taught the pieces first, now combine them
- **MAJOR MILESTONE**: First non-present tense introduced!

---

### Unit 30: Progressive Tenses - Estar + Gerund (Estou Fazendo)

**New vocabulary:**
- **Progressive expressions:**
  - agora (now)
  - neste momento (at this moment)
  - agora mesmo (right now)
  - atualmente (currently)
  - no momento (at the moment)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Progressive tense: ESTAR + GERUND:**
  - Expresses actions in progress (ongoing right now)
  - "I am doing", "You are working", "We are eating"
  - Very common in Brazilian Portuguese

**Forming the gerund:**

**-AR verbs: remove -ar, add -ando:**
- falar → fal**ando** (speaking)
- trabalhar → trabalh**ando** (working)
- estudar → estud**ando** (studying)
- cozinhar → cozinh**ando** (cooking)

**-ER verbs: remove -er, add -endo:**
- comer → com**endo** (eating)
- beber → beb**endo** (drinking)
- fazer → faz**endo** (doing/making)
- escrever → escrev**endo** (writing)

**-IR verbs: remove -ir, add -indo:**
- abrir → abr**indo** (opening)
- dormir → dorm**indo** (sleeping)
- assistir → assist**indo** (watching)
- sair → sa**indo** (leaving/going out)

**Structure: ESTAR (conjugated) + GERUND**
- Eu **estou** trabalhando. (I am working.)
- Você **está** comendo. (You are eating.)
- Ele **está** dormindo. (He is sleeping.)
- Nós **estamos** estudando. (We are studying.)
- Vocês **estão** assistindo TV. (You all are watching TV.)
- Eles **estão** falando. (They are talking.)

**When to use progressive:**
- Actions happening RIGHT NOW: "O que você está fazendo?" (What are you doing?)
- Temporary situations: "Estou morando em São Paulo." (I'm living in São Paulo - temporarily)
- Emphasis on ongoing action: "Estou trabalhando!" (I'm working! - can't be interrupted)

**Practice format:**
- Form gerunds from infinitives: falar → falando
- Conjugate estar + gerund: "Eu estou comendo"
- Answer "O que você está fazendo?"
- Describe what others are doing
- Use with "agora" and time expressions

**Student can now:**
- Form the gerund for all verb types (-ando, -endo, -indo)
- Use progressive tense for actions in progress
- Ask "O que você está fazendo?" (What are you doing?)
- Describe ongoing actions
- Distinguish simple present from progressive

**Typical sentences:**
- Eu estou trabalhando. (I am working.)
- O que você está fazendo? (What are you doing?)
- Ela está cozinhando. (She is cooking.)
- Nós estamos estudando português. (We are studying Portuguese.)
- Eles estão assistindo TV. (They are watching TV.)
- Estou falando no telefone. (I'm talking on the phone.)
- Ele está dormindo agora. (He is sleeping now.)

**Sample conversation:**
```
A: Alô? Oi! O que você está fazendo?
   (Hello? Hi! What are you doing?)
B: Estou cozinhando o jantar. E você?
   (I'm cooking dinner. And you?)

A: Eu estou assistindo um filme.
   (I'm watching a movie.)
B: Qual filme?
   (Which movie?)

A: Um filme brasileiro. É muito bom!
   (A Brazilian movie. It's very good!)
B: Legal! Bom, eu preciso ir. Ainda estou cozinhando.
   (Cool! Well, I need to go. I'm still cooking.)
```

**Common Mistakes to Avoid:**
- ❌ "Eu estou falar" (wrong - missing gerund ending)
- ✅ "Eu estou falando" (correct)
- ❌ "Eu sou trabalhando" (wrong - use ESTAR not SER)
- ✅ "Eu estou trabalhando" (correct)
- ❌ "falendo" (wrong ending for -AR verb)
- ✅ "falando" (correct - -AR verbs use -ando)

**Gerund Formation - Summary:**

**-AR verbs → -ANDO:**
- falar → fal**ando**
- trabalhar → trabalh**ando**
- estudar → estud**ando**
- jogar → jog**ando**
- comprar → compr**ando**

**-ER verbs → -ENDO:**
- comer → com**endo**
- beber → beb**endo**
- fazer → faz**endo**
- vender → vend**endo**
- escrever → escrev**endo**

**-IR verbs → -INDO:**
- abrir → abr**indo**
- dormir → dorm**indo**
- assistir → assist**indo**
- partir → part**indo**
- sair → sa**indo**

**Progressive Tense Conjugation:**

Using "trabalhar" (to work) as example:

- Eu **estou trabalhando** (I am working)
- Você **está trabalhando** (You are working)
- Ele/Ela **está trabalhando** (He/She is working)
- Nós **estamos trabalhando** (We are working)
- Vocês **estão trabalhando** (You all are working)
- Eles/Elas **estão trabalhando** (They are working)

**Simple Present vs Progressive:**

**Simple Present (habitual):**
- Eu trabalho todos os dias. (I work every day.)
- General habit, routine

**Progressive (right now):**
- Eu estou trabalhando agora. (I am working now.)
- Action happening at this moment

**Both are correct but different meanings!**

**Common Questions with Progressive:**
- O que você está fazendo? (What are you doing?)
- Onde você está indo? (Where are you going?)
- Com quem você está falando? (Who are you talking to?)
- Por que você está chorando? (Why are you crying?)

**Progressive in Past (preview for later unit):**
- Eu estava trabalhando. (I was working.)
- Uses imperfect of ESTAR + gerund
- Will be covered in future unit

**Negative Progressive:**
- Eu não estou trabalhando. (I am not working.)
- Structure: NÃO + estar + gerund

**Emphasis and Style:**
Progressive emphasizes the ongoing nature:
- "Eu trabalho" (neutral: I work)
- "Eu estou trabalhando" (emphasis: I'm working - busy, can't be interrupted)

**Brazilian vs European Portuguese:**
- **Brazilian:** Uses progressive VERY commonly
- **European:** Uses simple present more often
- This course teaches Brazilian Portuguese

**Alternative Structure (less common in Brazilian):**
- Estar **a** + infinitive (European Portuguese)
- Estou **a** trabalhar. (I am working - European)
- Brazilian: Estou trabalhando. (more common)

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- Unit 12: ESTAR → now using with gerund
- All verb units → forming gerunds from these verbs
- Unit 62: Daily activities → "Estou tomando banho" (I'm showering)
- Unit 38: Questions → "O que você está fazendo?"

**Key Learning:**
- Progressive tense: ESTAR + gerund (-ando, -endo, -indo)
- Expresses actions in progress RIGHT NOW
- Very common in Brazilian Portuguese
- -AR → -ando, -ER → -endo, -IR → -indo
- Essential for describing what's happening now

**Why This Unit:**
- **FOUNDATIONAL:** Progressive is extremely common in Brazilian Portuguese
- Natural progression: know present tense, now add progressive
- Ultra-granular: focuses ONLY on progressive formation
- Practical: immediate use for describing current actions
- Grammar milestone: important tense not yet covered

---

### Unit 31: Plural Possessives: Meus/Minhas (My - Plural)
**New vocabulary:**
- **meus/minhas** (my - masculine/feminine PLURAL) - extending Unit 14's meu/minha
- Plural family/friends:
  - irmãos/irmãs (brothers/sisters)
  - filhos/filhas (sons/daughters)
  - amigos/amigas (friends)
  - pais (parents - always masculine plural)
- Personal items (plural):
  - livros (books) - masculine plural
  - chaves (keys) - feminine plural
  - documentos (documents) - masculine plural
  - sapatos (shoes) - masculine plural

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Extending Unit 14:** Adding PLURAL forms meus/minhas to complete "my" system
- **Four forms total for "my":**
  - Masculine singular: **meu** pai (from Unit 14)
  - Feminine singular: **minha** mãe (from Unit 14)
  - Masculine plural: **meus** irmãos (NEW!)
  - Feminine plural: **minhas** irmãs (NEW!)
- **Agreement rule (review from Unit 14):** Possessive agrees with the THING POSSESSED
- Position: possessive + noun (no article needed)

**Practice format:**
- Review from Unit 14: "Meu pai mora em São Paulo", "Minha mãe trabalha na escola"
- **NEW - Masculine plural:** "Meus irmãos moram aqui" (My brothers live here)
- **NEW - Feminine plural:** "Minhas irmãs falam inglês" (My sisters speak English)
- **NEW - Parents:** "Meus pais moram no Rio" (My parents live in Rio)
- **NEW - Things (fem plural):** "Minhas chaves estão na mesa" (My keys are on the table)
- **NEW - Things (masc plural):** "Meus livros são novos" (My books are new)

**Student can now:**
- **Complete the "my" possessive system:** meu/minha/meus/minhas
- Talk about family members in plural (meus irmãos, minhas irmãs, meus pais)
- Express possession of multiple items (meus livros, minhas chaves)
- Understand full gender AND number agreement for possessives
- Apply all four forms correctly based on the noun

**Typical sentences:**
- Review: Meu pai é brasileiro (My father is Brazilian - from Unit 14)
- Review: Minha mãe trabalha no hospital (My mother works at the hospital - from Unit 14)
- **NEW:** Meus irmãos moram em São Paulo (My brothers live in São Paulo)
- **NEW:** Minhas irmãs falam inglês (My sisters speak English)
- **NEW:** Meus pais moram no Rio (My parents live in Rio)
- **NEW:** Meus amigos são brasileiros (My friends are Brazilian)
- **NEW:** Minhas chaves estão aqui (My keys are here)
- **NEW:** Meus livros são novos (My books are new)

**Complete "My" Possessive System:**
| Gender/Number | Form | Example | Translation |
|---------------|------|---------|-------------|
| Masc. Singular | meu | meu pai | my father |
| Fem. Singular | minha | minha mãe | my mother |
| Masc. Plural | meus | meus irmãos | my brothers |
| Fem. Plural | minhas | minhas irmãs | my sisters |

**Agreement Examples:**
- o livro → **meu** livro (masculine singular noun → masculine singular possessive)
- a casa → **minha** casa (feminine singular noun → feminine singular possessive)
- os livros → **meus** livros (masculine plural noun → masculine plural possessive)
- as casas → **minhas** casas (feminine plural noun → feminine plural possessive)

**Common Patterns:**
- Singular (from Unit 14): meu pai, minha mãe, meu amigo, minha amiga
- **Plural (NEW):** meus pais, minhas irmãs, meus amigos, minhas chaves

**Sample Conversation:**
- A: Onde moram seus pais? (Where do your parents live? - você form preview)
- B: Meus pais moram no Rio. (My parents live in Rio.)
- A: E seus irmãos? (And your brothers?)
- B: Meus irmãos moram comigo em São Paulo. (My brothers live with me in São Paulo.)
- A: Você tem muitos amigos? (Do you have many friends?)
- B: Sim, meus amigos são de São Paulo. (Yes, my friends are from São Paulo.)

**Common Mistakes to Avoid:**
- ❌ "Meu irmãs" (wrong - irmãs is feminine plural)
- ✅ "Minhas irmãs" (correct)
- ❌ "Minhas pais" (wrong - pais is masculine plural)
- ✅ "Meus pais" (correct)
- ❌ "Minha livros" (wrong - livros is masculine plural)
- ✅ "Meus livros" (correct)

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- **Unit 14:** Introduced meu/minha (singular) - now adding plural forms
- **Unit 16:** Used with possessions - "Tenho um cachorro. Meu cachorro..." → Now: "Meus cachorros..."
- **Unit 13:** Used with location - "na casa do meu irmão" → Now: "na casa dos meus pais"

**Key Learning:**
- **Four forms for "my":** meu/minha/meus/minhas
- Possessives agree with BOTH gender AND number of the thing possessed
- This completes the "my" possessive system
- Essential for talking about family in plural and multiple belongings

**Why This Unit:**
- Natural progression: extends Unit 14's singular possessives to plural
- Ultra-granular: adds ONLY plural forms of "my" (one concept)
- Essential before introducing other persons' possessives (your, his, her, our)
- Students master ONE person's complete system before moving to others
- Practical: enables richer conversation about family, friends, and belongings

---

### Unit 32: Your/His/Her Possessives: Seu/Sua + Dele/Dela Construction
**New vocabulary:**
- **seu/sua/seus/suas** (your/his/her - masculine/feminine, singular/plural) - **AMBIGUOUS!**
- **dele** (his - literally "of-him")
- **dela** (her - literally "of-her")
- **deles** (their - masculine/mixed group)
- **delas** (their - feminine group only)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Seu/sua/seus/suas possessives** - can mean YOUR, HIS, HER, or THEIR!
  - Four forms: seu (masc sing), sua (fem sing), seus (masc pl), suas (fem pl)
  - **CRITICAL PROBLEM:** Extremely ambiguous in Brazilian Portuguese
- **SOLUTION: Dele/Dela construction** (PREFERRED in colloquial BP!)
  - Structure: **article + noun + dele/dela/deles/delas**
  - o irmão dele (his brother), a casa dela (her house)
  - **REQUIRES article:** Cannot say just "irmão dele"
- Position:
  - Seu/sua: possessive + noun (like meu/minha)
  - Dele/dela: article + noun + dele/dela

**The Ambiguity Problem:**

⚠️ **MAJOR ISSUE:** "Seu irmão" can mean 5 different things!
- **Your** brother (você)
- **His** brother (ele)
- **Her** brother (ela)
- **Your (plural)** brother (vocês)
- **Their** brother (eles/elas)

**In conversation, this creates constant confusion!**

**Practice format - Seu/Sua (ambiguous):**
- "Seu pai mora aqui?" (Does your/his/her father live here?) - **AMBIGUOUS!**
- "Sua mãe trabalha?" (Does your/his/her mother work?) - **AMBIGUOUS!**
- "Seus irmãos falam inglês?" (Do your/his/her brothers speak English?) - **AMBIGUOUS!**

**Practice format - Dele/Dela (CLEAR):**
- "O pai dele mora aqui?" (Does HIS father live here?) - **CLEAR!**
- "A mãe dela trabalha?" (Does HER mother work?) - **CLEAR!**
- "Os irmãos dele falam inglês?" (Do HIS brothers speak English?) - **CLEAR!**

**Student can now:**
- Use seu/sua/seus/suas possessives (but understand the ambiguity)
- **Use dele/dela/deles/delas construction for clarity** (PREFERRED in BP!)
- Distinguish "your" from "his/her" using context or dele/dela
- Understand why Brazilians prefer the dele/dela construction
- Express third-person possession clearly

**Typical sentences with seu/sua:**
- Seu irmão mora aqui? (Does your/his/her brother live here?)
- Sua casa é grande? (Is your/his/her house big?)
- Seus amigos são brasileiros? (Are your/his/her friends Brazilian?)
- Suas chaves estão na mesa (Your/His/Her keys are on the table)

**Typical sentences with dele/dela (PREFERRED):**
- O irmão dele mora no Rio (HIS brother lives in Rio) - **CLEAR!**
- A casa dela é grande (HER house is big) - **CLEAR!**
- Os amigos dele são brasileiros (HIS friends are Brazilian) - **CLEAR!**
- As amigas delas trabalham aqui (THEIR (fem) friends work here) - **CLEAR!**

**Comparison - Ambiguous vs Clear:**
| Ambiguous (seu/sua) | Clear (dele/dela) | Meaning |
|---------------------|-------------------|---------|
| Seu carro é novo | O carro dele é novo | HIS car is new |
| Seu carro é novo | O carro dela é novo | HER car is new |
| Sua casa é grande | A casa dele é grande | HIS house is big |
| Sua casa é grande | A casa dela é grande | HER house is big |

**When to use which:**
- **Use meu/minha/meus/minhas** for "my" - always clear (from Units 14 & 27)
- **Use dele/dela/deles/delas** for "his/her/their" - clearest option! **PREFERRED in BP!**
- **Use seu/sua/seus/suas** for "your" (você/vocês) - but can still be ambiguous

**CRITICAL: Dele/Dela REQUIRES article:**
- ❌ "irmão dele" (WRONG - missing article)
- ✅ "o irmão dele" (CORRECT - with article)
- ❌ "casa dela" (WRONG - missing article)
- ✅ "a casa dela" (CORRECT - with article)

**Full Possessive System So Far:**
| Person | Masc. Sing. | Fem. Sing. | Masc. Plural | Fem. Plural |
|--------|-------------|------------|--------------|-------------|
| eu (my) | meu pai | minha mãe | meus irmãos | minhas irmãs |
| você/ele/ela (your/his/her) - AMBIGUOUS | seu pai | sua mãe | seus irmãos | suas irmãs |
| ele (his) - CLEAR | o pai dele | a mãe dele | os irmãos dele | as irmãs dele |
| ela (her) - CLEAR | o pai dela | a mãe dela | os irmãos dela | as irmãs dela |

**Common in BP Speech:**
- "Vi o carro dele ontem" (I saw his car yesterday) - **VERY COMMON**
- "Conheço a irmã dela" (I know her sister) - **VERY COMMON**
- "Gosto dos amigos deles" (I like their friends) - **VERY COMMON**
- "A mãe dela mora no Rio" (Her mother lives in Rio) - **VERY COMMON**

**Sample Conversation:**
- A: Onde mora o irmão dele? (Where does his brother live?)
- B: O irmão dele mora em São Paulo. (His brother lives in São Paulo.)
- A: E a irmã dela? (And her sister?)
- B: A irmã dela mora no Rio. (Her sister lives in Rio.)
- A: Os pais deles moram juntos? (Do their parents live together?)
- B: Não, o pai dele mora aqui, mas a mãe dela mora lá. (No, his father lives here, but her mother lives there.)

**Common Mistakes to Avoid:**
- ❌ "irmão dele" (wrong - missing article)
- ✅ "o irmão dele" (correct)
- ❌ "o seu irmão dele" (wrong - redundant: don't mix seu with dele)
- ✅ "o irmão dele" (correct) OR "seu irmão" (correct but ambiguous)
- ❌ "dele casa" (wrong - wrong word order)
- ✅ "a casa dele" (correct - article + noun + dele)

**Agreement with Dele/Dela:**
The article and noun agree with the thing possessed:
- **o** irmão dele (masculine singular noun → o)
- **a** casa dela (feminine singular noun → a)
- **os** amigos dele (masculine plural noun → os)
- **as** chaves dela (feminine plural noun → as)

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- **Unit 14:** meu/minha (my - singular)
- **Unit 27:** meus/minhas (my - plural)
- **Unit 28:** seu/sua + dele/dela (your/his/her) - completes third-person possession
- **Unit 33 (next):** nosso/nossa (our)

**Key Learning:**
- **Seu/sua is VERY ambiguous** - can mean your, his, her, or their
- **Dele/dela construction is PREFERRED in Brazilian Portuguese** for clarity
- Dele/dela ALWAYS requires the article before the noun
- This is essential for talking about HIS/HER family, friends, and belongings
- Students should favor dele/dela in speech to avoid confusion

**Why This Unit:**
- Critical for clear communication - ambiguity is a real problem in BP
- Ultra-granular: focuses on one possessive person (your/his/her) + the solution
- Teaches REAL Brazilian Portuguese usage, not just textbook forms
- Essential before past tense narratives (talking about "his friends," "her parents")
- Prepares for "our" possessives in next unit

---

### Unit 33: Our Possessives: Nosso/Nossa/Nossos/Nossas
**New vocabulary:**
- **nosso/nossa/nossos/nossas** (our - masculine/feminine, singular/plural)
- Words commonly used with "our":
  - família (family) - feminine
  - casa (house) - feminine
  - país (country) - masculine
  - cidade (city) - feminine
  - trabalho (job/work) - masculine
  - projeto (project) - masculine

**Grammar introduced:**
- **"Our" possessive adjectives: nosso/nossa/nossos/nossas**
  - Four forms based on gender/number of noun:
    - **nosso** = our (masculine singular): nosso pai
    - **nossa** = our (feminine singular): nossa mãe
    - **nossos** = our (masculine plural): nossos irmãos
    - **nossas** = our (feminine plural): nossas irmãs
- **Agreement rule (same as all possessives):** agrees with the THING POSSESSED
- Position: possessive + noun (no article needed)
- **No ambiguity!** - nosso/nossa ALWAYS means "our" (unlike seu/sua)

**Practice format:**
- "Nossa casa é grande" (Our house is big)
- "Nosso pai mora em São Paulo" (Our father lives in São Paulo)
- "Nossos amigos são brasileiros" (Our friends are Brazilian)
- "Nossas chaves estão na mesa" (Our keys are on the table)
- "Nossa família é grande" (Our family is big)
- "Nosso trabalho é difícil" (Our work is difficult)

**Student can now:**
- Express "our" possession with full gender/number agreement
- Use all four forms correctly (nosso/nossa/nossos/nossas)
- **Complete the possessive system:** my, your/his/her, our
- Talk about shared family, belongings, and experiences
- Combine with nós (we) for complete first-person plural expression

**Typical sentences:**
- Nossa casa é pequena (Our house is small)
- Nosso pai trabalha no banco (Our father works at the bank)
- Nossa mãe é professora (Our mother is a teacher)
- Nossos pais moram no Rio (Our parents live in Rio)
- Nossos irmãos falam inglês (Our brothers speak English)
- Nossas irmãs moram aqui (Our sisters live here)
- Nossos amigos são legais (Our friends are cool)
- Nossa cidade é bonita (Our city is beautiful)

**Complete "Our" Possessive System:**
| Gender/Number | Form | Example | Translation |
|---------------|------|---------|-------------|
| Masc. Singular | nosso | nosso pai | our father |
| Fem. Singular | nossa | nossa mãe | our mother |
| Masc. Plural | nossos | nossos irmãos | our brothers |
| Fem. Plural | nossas | nossas irmãs | our sisters |

**Agreement Examples:**
- o pai → **nosso** pai (masculine singular noun → nosso)
- a mãe → **nossa** mãe (feminine singular noun → nossa)
- os irmãos → **nossos** irmãos (masculine plural noun → nossos)
- as irmãs → **nossas** irmãs (feminine plural noun → nossas)

**Combining with Nós (we) from Unit 22:**
- **Nós moramos** em São Paulo. **Nossa casa** é grande. (We live in São Paulo. Our house is big.)
- **Nossos pais** moram no Rio, mas **nós moramos** aqui. (Our parents live in Rio, but we live here.)
- **Trabalhamos** juntos. **Nosso trabalho** é difícil. (We work together. Our work is difficult.)

**Full Possessive System - COMPLETE:**
| Person | Masc. Sing. | Fem. Sing. | Masc. Plural | Fem. Plural |
|--------|-------------|------------|--------------|-------------|
| eu (my) | meu pai | minha mãe | meus irmãos | minhas irmãs |
| você/ele/ela (ambiguous) | seu pai | sua mãe | seus irmãos | suas irmãs |
| ele (his - clear) | o pai dele | a mãe dele | os irmãos dele | as irmãs dele |
| ela (her - clear) | o pai dela | a mãe dela | os irmãos dela | as irmãs dela |
| nós (our) | nosso pai | nossa mãe | nossos irmãos | nossas irmãs |

**Sample Conversation:**
- A: Onde moram seus pais? (Where do your parents live?)
- B: Nossos pais moram no Rio, mas nós moramos aqui em São Paulo. (Our parents live in Rio, but we live here in São Paulo.)
- A: E seus irmãos? (And your siblings?)
- B: Nossos irmãos moram com nossos pais no Rio. (Our siblings live with our parents in Rio.)
- A: Como é sua casa? (What's your house like?)
- B: Nossa casa é pequena, mas nossa cidade é linda. (Our house is small, but our city is beautiful.)

**Common Patterns:**
- Nossa + feminine singular: nossa casa, nossa família, nossa cidade, nossa mãe
- Nosso + masculine singular: nosso pai, nosso país, nosso trabalho, nosso irmão
- Nossas + feminine plural: nossas irmãs, nossas chaves, nossas amigas
- Nossos + masculine plural: nossos pais, nossos amigos, nossos irmãos

**Common Mistakes to Avoid:**
- ❌ "Nosso mãe" (wrong - mãe is feminine)
- ✅ "Nossa mãe" (correct)
- ❌ "Nossa pai" (wrong - pai is masculine)
- ✅ "Nosso pai" (correct)
- ❌ "Nosso irmãs" (wrong - irmãs is feminine plural)
- ✅ "Nossas irmãs" (correct)
- ❌ "Nossas pais" (wrong - pais is masculine plural)
- ✅ "Nossos pais" (correct)

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- **Unit 14:** meu/minha (my - singular)
- **Unit 22:** nós (we) - now can say "we" AND "our"
- **Unit 27:** meus/minhas (my - plural)
- **Unit 28:** seu/sua + dele/dela (your/his/her)
- **Unit 29:** nosso/nossa (our) - **COMPLETES possessive system for main persons!**

**Key Learning:**
- **Four forms for "our":** nosso/nossa/nossos/nossas
- Possessives agree with BOTH gender AND number of the thing possessed
- **No ambiguity** - nosso/nossa ALWAYS means "our" (clearer than seu/sua!)
- Essential for talking about shared family, home, and experiences
- **MILESTONE:** Complete possessive system for eu, você/ele/ela, nós

**Why This Unit:**
- Natural progression: completes the possessive system after my, your/his/her
- Ultra-granular: introduces ONLY "our" possessives (one concept)
- Essential for first-person plural communication - pairs perfectly with nós from Unit 25
- Practical: enables talking about shared family, home, work, and experiences
- **MILESTONE:** Students now have complete possessive system for all main persons!

---

### Unit 34: Past Tense - Regular -AR Verbs (Preterite)
**New vocabulary:**
- **ontem** (yesterday)
- **na semana passada** (last week)
- **no mês passado** (last month)
- **no ano passado** (last year)
- **anteontem** (the day before yesterday)
- **há [time]** (ago) - há dois dias (two days ago)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Preterite tense for regular -AR verbs** (simple past - completed actions)
- Past tense endings for -AR verbs:
  - eu: -**ei** (morei, trabalhei, estudei)
  - você/ele/ela: -**ou** (morou, trabalhou, estudou)
  - nós: -**amos** (moramos, trabalhamos, estudamos) - **SAME as present!**
  - vocês/eles/elas: -**aram** (moraram, trabalharam, estudaram)
- Used for actions that happened at a specific time in the past and are complete
- Time expressions that signal past tense

**Practice format:**
- Present: "Moro em São Paulo" → Past: "Morei em São Paulo" (I lived in São Paulo)
- Present: "Trabalho no banco" → Past: "Trabalhei no banco ontem" (I worked at the bank yesterday)
- Present: "Estudo português" → Past: "Estudei português na semana passada" (I studied Portuguese last week)
- Questions: "Onde você morou?" (Where did you live?)

**Student can now:**
- Talk about completed past actions with regular -AR verbs
- Use all -AR verbs learned so far in past tense
- Distinguish present from past using time expressions
- Notice that nós form is SAME in present and past (context determines meaning)
- Ask questions about past events

**Typical sentences:**
- Morei no Brasil (I lived in Brazil)
- Trabalhei ontem (I worked yesterday)
- Estudei português na semana passada (I studied Portuguese last week)
- Ele morou em São Paulo (He lived in São Paulo)
- Nós trabalhamos ontem (We worked yesterday - same as present!)
- Eles falaram português (They spoke Portuguese)
- Você gostou do filme? (Did you like the movie?)
- Não gostei (I didn't like it)

**Full Conjugation - Preterite -AR Verbs:**
| Pronoun | Present | Preterite | Example (morar) |
|---------|---------|-----------|-----------------|
| eu | moro | morei | Morei no Rio |
| você/ele/ela | mora | morou | Ele morou aqui |
| nós | moramos | moramos | Moramos lá |
| vocês/eles/elas | moram | moraram | Eles moraram aqui |

**Pattern for All -AR Verbs in Preterite:**
- morar: morei, morou, moramos, moraram
- trabalhar: trabalhei, trabalhou, trabalhamos, trabalharam
- estudar: estudei, estudou, estudamos, estudaram
- falar: falei, falou, falamos, falaram
- gostar: gostei, gostou, gostamos, gostaram
- andar: andei, andou, andamos, andaram
- viajar: viajei, viajou, viajamos, viajaram

**Key Pattern Recognition:**
- Remove -ar, add: -ei, -ou, -amos, -aram
- **nós form identical to present:** "Moramos" can mean "we live" OR "we lived" (context clarifies)
- All other forms clearly signal past tense

**With Time Expressions:**
- Morei em São Paulo **no ano passado** (I lived in São Paulo last year)
- Trabalhei **ontem** (I worked yesterday)
- Estudamos português **na semana passada** (We studied Portuguese last week)
- Ele falou comigo **há dois dias** (He spoke with me two days ago)
- Não trabalhei **anteontem** (I didn't work the day before yesterday)

**Comparing Present and Past:**
- Present: Moro em São Paulo agora (I live in São Paulo now)
- Past: Morei em São Paulo no ano passado (I lived in São Paulo last year)
- Present: Trabalho no banco (I work at the bank)
- Past: Trabalhei no banco ontem (I worked at the bank yesterday)

**Sample Conversation:**
- A: Onde você morou antes? (Where did you live before?)
- B: Morei no Rio. (I lived in Rio.)
- A: Você gostou? (Did you like it?)
- B: Sim, gostei muito. (Yes, I liked it a lot.)
- A: Você trabalhou lá? (Did you work there?)
- B: Sim, trabalhei em um banco. (Yes, I worked at a bank.)

**With Negation (from Unit 14):**
- Não morei no Brasil (I didn't live in Brazil)
- Ele não trabalhou ontem (He didn't work yesterday)
- Não gostamos do filme (We didn't like the movie)
- Eles não estudaram (They didn't study)

**Key Learning:**
- This is the **simple past tense** (preterite) - for completed actions
- Very regular pattern for -AR verbs (the most common verb type)
- Easy to form: just change the ending
- Students can now talk about PAST experiences with -AR verbs
- Nós form creates interesting ambiguity: "Moramos aqui" = "We live here" or "We lived here"

**Why This Unit:**
- Natural progression: present → future → past
- -AR verbs are the most common and were taught first
- Regular pattern makes it accessible
- Immediate practical value - telling stories about past events
- Ultra-granular: focusing only on regular -AR verbs (not -ER/-IR yet, not irregulars)
- Students can now describe past actions with 5+ -AR verbs they already know
- **MAJOR MILESTONE**: First true past tense introduced!

**Note:** Irregular past tense verbs (fui, foi, teve, etc.) will come in future units. This unit focuses exclusively on the regular -AR pattern.

---

### Unit 35: Past Tense - Regular -ER/-IR Verbs (Preterite)
**New vocabulary:**
- Time expressions (review from Unit 29): ontem, na semana passada, no mês passado
- Additional: de manhã (in the morning), à tarde (in the afternoon), à noite (at night)
- já (already), ainda não (not yet)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Preterite tense for regular -ER and -IR verbs**
- **KEY INSIGHT: -ER and -IR verbs share the SAME past tense endings!**
- Past tense endings for -ER/-IR verbs:
  - eu: -**i** (comi, bebi, corri, abri, parti, assisti)
  - você/ele/ela: -**eu/-iu** (comeu, bebeu, correu, abriu, partiu, assistiu)
  - nós: -**emos/-imos** (comemos/abrimos - same as present!)
  - vocês/eles/elas: -**eram/-iram** (comeram/abriram)
- Used for completed actions in the past (same as -AR verbs in Unit 29)

**Practice format:**
- Present: "Como arroz" → Past: "Comi arroz ontem" (I ate rice yesterday)
- Present: "Bebo café" → Past: "Bebi café de manhã" (I drank coffee in the morning)
- Present: "Assisto filmes" → Past: "Assisti um filme ontem" (I watched a movie yesterday)
- Questions: "O que você comeu?" (What did you eat?)

**Student can now:**
- Talk about completed past actions with regular -ER and -IR verbs
- Use all -ER verbs from Unit 20 in past tense (comer, beber, correr)
- Use all -IR verbs from Unit 26 in past tense (abrir, partir, assistir)
- Recognize that -ER and -IR share past tense endings
- Notice that nós form is SAME as present (like -AR verbs)
- Combine with -AR past tense from Unit 29

**Typical sentences:**
- Comi arroz e feijão ontem (I ate rice and beans yesterday)
- Bebi café de manhã (I drank coffee in the morning)
- Corri no parque na semana passada (I ran in the park last week)
- Abri a porta (I opened the door)
- Ele partiu cedo (He left early)
- Assistimos um filme (We watched a movie)
- Vocês comeram? (Did you all eat?)
- Não bebi cerveja (I didn't drink beer)

**Full Conjugation - Preterite -ER/-IR Verbs:**
| Pronoun | -ER (comer) | -IR (abrir) | Pattern |
|---------|-------------|-------------|---------|
| eu | comi | abri | -i |
| você/ele/ela | comeu | abriu | -eu/-iu |
| nós | comemos | abrimos | -emos/-imos |
| vocês/eles/elas | comeram | abriram | -eram/-iram |

**Pattern for -ER Verbs in Preterite:**
- comer: comi, comeu, comemos, comeram
- beber: bebi, bebeu, bebemos, beberam
- correr: corri, correu, corremos, correram

**Pattern for -IR Verbs in Preterite:**
- abrir: abri, abriu, abrimos, abriram
- partir: parti, partiu, partimos, partiram
- assistir: assisti, assistiu, assistimos, assistiram

**Key Pattern Recognition:**
- **-ER and -IR verbs share the same past tense pattern!**
- Remove -er/-ir, add: -i, -eu/-iu, -emos/-imos, -eram/-iram
- **nós form identical to present** (just like -AR verbs):
  - "Comemos" = "we eat" OR "we ate" (context clarifies)
  - "Abrimos" = "we open" OR "we opened" (context clarifies)
- Other forms clearly signal past tense

**Comparing All Three Verb Types in Past:**
| Verb Type | eu | você/ele/ela | nós | vocês/eles/elas |
|-----------|-----|--------------|-----|-----------------|
| -AR (morar) | morei | morou | moramos | moraram |
| -ER (comer) | comi | comeu | comemos | comeram |
| -IR (abrir) | abri | abriu | abrimos | abriram |

**Comparing Present and Past (-ER/-IR):**
- Present: Como arroz todo dia (I eat rice every day)
- Past: Comi arroz ontem (I ate rice yesterday)
- Present: Assisto filmes (I watch movies)
- Past: Assisti um filme na semana passada (I watched a movie last week)
- Present: Bebo café de manhã (I drink coffee in the morning)
- Past: Bebi café ontem de manhã (I drank coffee yesterday morning)

**Sample Conversation:**
- A: O que você comeu ontem? (What did you eat yesterday?)
- B: Comi peixe e salada. (I ate fish and salad.)
- A: Você bebeu vinho? (Did you drink wine?)
- B: Não, bebi água. (No, I drank water.)
- A: Vocês assistiram o filme? (Did you all watch the movie?)
- B: Sim, assistimos ontem à noite. (Yes, we watched it last night.)

**Combining with -AR Past (Unit 29):**
- Trabalhei ontem e depois comi no restaurante (I worked yesterday and then ate at the restaurant)
- Estudei português de manhã e à tarde corri no parque (I studied Portuguese in the morning and in the afternoon I ran in the park)
- Eles moraram no Brasil e comeram muito churrasco (They lived in Brazil and ate a lot of barbecue)

**With Negation:**
- Não comi carne (I didn't eat meat)
- Ele não bebeu cerveja (He didn't drink beer)
- Não assistimos o filme (We didn't watch the movie)
- Eles não abriram a loja (They didn't open the store)

**Key Learning:**
- **-ER and -IR verbs share identical past tense conjugations**
- This simplifies learning - only need to memorize one pattern for two verb types
- Regular pattern makes it accessible
- Students can now talk about eating, drinking, watching in the past
- Combined with Unit 29, students have past tense for ALL regular verb types

**Why This Unit:**
- Natural progression: -AR past (Unit 29) → -ER/-IR past (Unit 31)
- Shows the elegance: -ER and -IR merge in past tense
- Ultra-granular: still only regular verbs (irregulars come later)
- Immediate practical value - talking about meals, activities
- Students can now use past tense with 11+ verbs they already know
- **MAJOR MILESTONE**: Complete regular verb system in past tense!

**Note:** Irregular past tense verbs (fui, foi, fiz, teve, etc.) will come in Unit 32. This unit focuses exclusively on regular -ER and -IR patterns.

---

### Unit 36: Past Tense - Essential Irregular Verbs (ser, ir, ter, estar)
**New vocabulary:**
- Time expressions (review): ontem, na semana passada, no ano passado
- Additional time expressions:
  - no passado (in the past)
  - quando (when)
  - antes (before)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Preterite tense for the most essential irregular verbs**
- **AMAZING FACT: ser (to be) and ir (to go) share identical past tense forms!**
- Four essential irregulars:
  - **ser/ir**: fui, foi, fomos, foram
  - **ter**: tive, teve, tivemos, tiveram
  - **estar**: estive, esteve, estivemos, estiveram
- Context determines meaning for ser vs ir (both use fui, foi, etc.)
- These verbs don't follow regular patterns - must be memorized

**Practice format:**
- Present: "Sou brasileiro" → Past: "Fui brasileiro" (doesn't make sense - identity doesn't change!)
- Better: "Sou professor" → Past: "Fui professor no ano passado" (I was a teacher last year)
- Present: "Vou ao trabalho" → Past: "Fui ao trabalho ontem" (I went to work yesterday)
- Present: "Tenho um carro" → Past: "Tive um carro" (I had a car)
- Present: "Estou em casa" → Past: "Estive em casa ontem" (I was at home yesterday)

**Student can now:**
- Talk about past identity/professions (fui)
- Talk about where they went (fui)
- Distinguish ser/ir by context
- Talk about past possession (tive)
- Talk about past location/state (estive)
- Tell complete stories combining regular and irregular verbs

**Typical sentences:**
- Fui professor no Brasil (I was a teacher in Brazil) - ser
- Fui ao cinema ontem (I went to the movies yesterday) - ir
- Ela foi brasileira (She was Brazilian) - doesn't work! Identity doesn't change
- Ele foi ao banco (He went to the bank) - ir
- Fomos ao restaurante (We went to the restaurant) - ir
- Tive um cachorro (I had a dog)
- Não tive tempo (I didn't have time)
- Estive em São Paulo (I was in São Paulo)
- Estivemos cansados (We were tired)

**Full Conjugation - Essential Irregulars:**
| Pronoun | ser/ir | ter | estar |
|---------|---------|-----|-------|
| eu | fui | tive | estive |
| você/ele/ela | foi | teve | esteve |
| nós | fomos | tivemos | estivemos |
| vocês/eles/elas | foram | tiveram | estiveram |

**Ser vs Ir - Context is Key:**
- **Ser (was/were):**
  - Fui estudante (I was a student)
  - Ele foi professor (He was a teacher)
  - Fomos felizes (We were happy)
  - Context: identity, profession, characteristics

- **Ir (went):**
  - Fui ao trabalho (I went to work)
  - Ele foi ao Brasil (He went to Brazil)
  - Fomos de ônibus (We went by bus)
  - Context: movement, destinations, going somewhere

**Common Patterns:**
- **fui/foi + profession:** "Fui professor" (I was a teacher)
- **fui/foi + a/ao/à:** "Fui ao banco" (I went to the bank) - clearly ir
- **fui/foi + de:** "Fui de carro" (I went by car) - clearly ir
- **tive + noun:** "Tive aulas" (I had classes)
- **estive + location:** "Estive em casa" (I was at home)
- **estive + state:** "Estive doente" (I was sick)

**Comparing Present and Past:**
| Verb | Present (eu) | Past (eu) | Example |
|------|--------------|-----------|---------|
| ser | sou | fui | Sou professor → Fui professor |
| ir | vou | fui | Vou ao cinema → Fui ao cinema |
| ter | tenho | tive | Tenho tempo → Tive tempo |
| estar | estou | estive | Estou em casa → Estive em casa |

**Sample Conversation:**
- A: Onde você esteve ontem? (Where were you yesterday?)
- B: Estive em casa o dia todo. (I was at home all day.)
- A: Você foi ao trabalho na semana passada? (Did you go to work last week?)
- B: Não, tive férias. (No, I had vacation.)
- A: Você foi professor antes? (Were you a teacher before?)
- B: Sim, fui professor de inglês. (Yes, I was an English teacher.)

**Combining with Regular Past (Units 26-27):**
- Fui ao restaurante e comi peixe (I went to the restaurant and ate fish)
- Estive em casa e assisti um filme (I was at home and watched a movie)
- Tive aulas de português e estudei muito (I had Portuguese classes and studied a lot)
- Fomos ao parque e corremos (We went to the park and ran)

**With Negation:**
- Não fui ao trabalho (I didn't go to work)
- Ele não foi brasileiro (He wasn't Brazilian - rare, identity doesn't change)
- Não tive tempo (I didn't have time)
- Não estive lá (I wasn't there)
- Eles não foram ao cinema (They didn't go to the movies)

**Common Mistakes to Avoid:**
- ❌ Using "fui" for current identity: "Fui brasileiro" (I was Brazilian - implies you're not anymore!)
- ✅ Better: "Sou brasileiro" (I am Brazilian - present)
- ✅ Or: "Fui professor" (I was a teacher - professions can change)

**Key Learning:**
- **ser and ir share identical past forms** - only context clarifies meaning
- These four verbs are the most commonly used irregular verbs in Portuguese
- They appear in almost every conversation about the past
- Must be memorized - no pattern to help
- Students already know these verbs in present tense (Units 1, 8, 12, 14)

**Why This Unit:**
- Natural progression: regular past → irregular past
- Ultra-granular: focusing only on the 4 most essential irregulars
- Students already know these verbs in present tense
- Immediate practical value - these are THE most common verbs in past tense
- Enables much richer storytelling about the past
- **MAJOR MILESTONE**: Can now tell complete stories with both regular and irregular verbs!

**Note:** Other irregular verbs (fazer → fiz, ver → vi, dar → dei, etc.) will come in future units. This unit focuses on the four most essential irregulars that students already know in present tense.

---

### Unit 37: Past Tense - Common Irregular Verbs (fazer, ver, dar)
**New vocabulary:**
- Vocabulary that pairs with these verbs:
  - perguntas (questions)
  - trabalho (work/task)
  - exercícios (exercises)
  - presente (gift/present)
  - dinheiro (money)
  - ajuda (help)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Three more essential irregular verbs in preterite**
- **fazer (to make/do)**: fiz, fez, fizemos, fizeram
- **ver (to see/watch)**: vi, viu, vimos, viram
- **dar (to give)**: dei, deu, demos, deram
- These verbs are extremely common in past tense conversations
- Each has its own irregular pattern - must be memorized

**Practice format:**
- Present: "Faço exercícios" → Past: "Fiz exercícios ontem" (I did exercises yesterday)
- Present: "Vejo meus amigos" → Past: "Vi meus amigos" (I saw my friends)
- Present: "Dou presentes" → Past: "Dei um presente" (I gave a gift)
- Questions: "O que você fez ontem?" (What did you do yesterday?)

**Student can now:**
- Talk about what they did/made (fiz)
- Talk about what they saw/watched (vi)
- Talk about what they gave (dei)
- Answer "O que você fez?" (What did you do?) - one of the most common questions
- Combine with Units 26-28 for rich storytelling

**Typical sentences:**
- Fiz exercícios de manhã (I did exercises in the morning)
- Fiz o trabalho ontem (I did the work yesterday)
- Fiz uma pergunta (I asked a question)
- Vi meus amigos (I saw my friends)
- Vi um filme ontem (I saw/watched a movie yesterday)
- Não vi nada (I didn't see anything)
- Dei um presente para ela (I gave her a gift)
- Dei dinheiro (I gave money)
- Ele me deu ajuda (He gave me help)

**Full Conjugation - Common Irregulars:**
| Pronoun | fazer | ver | dar |
|---------|-------|-----|-----|
| eu | fiz | vi | dei |
| você/ele/ela | fez | viu | deu |
| nós | fizemos | vimos | demos |
| vocês/eles/elas | fizeram | viram | deram |

**Pattern Recognition (or lack thereof!):**
- **fazer**: fiz, fez, fizemos, fizeram
  - Note: z sound throughout
  - Stem changes completely from "faz-" to "fiz-/fez-"

- **ver**: vi, viu, vimos, viram
  - Very short forms (just 2-3 letters!)
  - Similar to regular -IR pattern but shorter

- **dar**: dei, deu, demos, deram
  - Looks somewhat like regular -ER verbs (dei/deu)
  - But it's from "dar" (ends in -ar)
  - Unique pattern

**Comparing Present and Past:**
| Verb | Present (eu) | Past (eu) | Example |
|------|--------------|-----------|---------|
| fazer | faço | fiz | Faço exercícios → Fiz exercícios |
| ver | vejo | vi | Vejo filmes → Vi um filme |
| dar | dou | dei | Dou presentes → Dei um presente |

**Common Uses for "fazer":**
- Fiz o trabalho (I did the work)
- Fiz exercícios (I did exercises)
- Fiz uma pergunta (I asked a question / literally: made a question)
- Fiz comida (I made food)
- O que você fez? (What did you do?) - **THE most common past tense question!**

**Common Uses for "ver":**
- Vi meus amigos (I saw my friends)
- Vi um filme (I watched a movie)
- Vi a casa (I saw the house)
- Não vi nada (I didn't see anything)
- Note: "ver" can mean both "to see" and "to watch"

**Common Uses for "dar":**
- Dei um presente (I gave a gift)
- Dei aulas (I gave classes / I taught)
- Dei dinheiro (I gave money)
- Ele me deu ajuda (He gave me help)
- Demos um passeio (We took a walk / literally: gave a walk)

**Sample Conversation:**
- A: O que você fez ontem? (What did you do yesterday?)
- B: Fiz exercícios de manhã e depois vi meus amigos. (I did exercises in the morning and then saw my friends.)
- A: Você viu o filme novo? (Did you see the new movie?)
- B: Sim, vi na semana passada. (Yes, I saw it last week.)
- A: Você deu o presente para ela? (Did you give her the gift?)
- B: Sim, dei ontem. (Yes, I gave it yesterday.)

**Combining with Previous Past Tense Units:**
- Fui ao cinema e vi um filme (I went to the movies and saw a film)
- Estive em casa, fiz o trabalho e depois assisti TV (I was at home, did work and then watched TV)
- Tive aulas de manhã, fiz exercícios e depois comi (I had classes in the morning, did exercises and then ate)
- Trabalhei muito, fiz todas as tarefas e não vi meus amigos (I worked a lot, did all the tasks and didn't see my friends)

**With Negation:**
- Não fiz nada ontem (I didn't do anything yesterday)
- Ele não viu o filme (He didn't see the movie)
- Não dei dinheiro (I didn't give money)
- Eles não fizeram o trabalho (They didn't do the work)
- Não vimos ninguém (We didn't see anyone)

**Key Phrases with "O que você fez?":**
This is THE most important question in past tense conversation:
- A: O que você fez ontem? (What did you do yesterday?)
- B: Fiz exercícios. (I did exercises.)
- B: Trabalhei. (I worked.)
- B: Vi meus amigos. (I saw my friends.)
- B: Não fiz nada. (I didn't do anything.)

**Key Learning:**
- These three verbs are among the most commonly used in daily conversation
- "O que você fez?" is essential - students will hear this constantly
- "fazer" is versatile - covers "do," "make," and many expressions
- "ver" covers both "see" and "watch"
- "dar" is essential for talking about giving, teaching, taking walks
- Combined with Units 26-28, students now have 7 past tense irregular verbs + all regular verbs

**Why This Unit:**
- Natural progression: essential irregulars (Unit 32) → common irregulars (Unit 33)
- Ultra-granular: only 3 new irregular verbs (manageable)
- Immediate practical value - "fazer" especially is used constantly
- "O que você fez?" is one of the most common questions students will encounter
- Enables much richer past tense conversation
- Students can now handle most basic past tense storytelling

**Note:** Additional irregular verbs (poder, querer, saber, trazer, dizer, etc.) can come in future units. This unit focuses on three that are immediately essential for basic conversation.

---

### Unit 38: Question Words (Interrogatives)
**New vocabulary:**
- **Question words (interrogatives):**
  - **o que / que** (what)
  - **quem** (who)
  - **onde** (where)
  - **quando** (when)
  - **como** (how)
  - **por que** (why)
  - **qual / quais** (which / which ones)
  - **quanto/a/os/as** (how much / how many)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Systematic introduction to interrogatives**
- Question formation with all tenses (present, future, past)
- Word order: interrogative + verb + subject (or just interrogative + verb with pro-drop)
- Using question words students have encountered informally since early units
- Questions can end with question mark but intonation is key

**Practice format:**
- Present: "O que você faz?" (What do you do?)
- Future: "Quando você vai viajar?" (When are you going to travel?)
- Past: "Onde você morou?" (Where did you live?)
- "Quem é ele?" (Who is he?)
- "Como você está?" (How are you?)
- "Por que você estuda português?" (Why do you study Portuguese?)

**Student can now:**
- Ask questions about any topic covered so far
- Use interrogatives with present, future, and past tenses
- Form information questions (not just yes/no questions)
- Understand that many question words they've seen informally are now systematic
- Conduct two-way conversations (not just answer, but also ask)

**Typical sentences:**
- O que você faz? (What do you do?)
- Quem é ela? (Who is she?)
- Onde você mora? (Where do you live?)
- Quando você vai viajar? (When are you going to travel?)
- Como você está? (How are you?)
- Por que você gosta de português? (Why do you like Portuguese?)
- Qual é seu nome? (What is your name? / literally: Which is your name?)
- Quanto custa? (How much does it cost?)
- Quantos irmãos você tem? (How many siblings do you have?)

**Full Question Word System:**
| Question Word | Meaning | Example |
|---------------|---------|---------|
| o que / que | what | O que você fez? (What did you do?) |
| quem | who | Quem é ele? (Who is he?) |
| onde | where | Onde você mora? (Where do you live?) |
| quando | when | Quando você foi? (When did you go?) |
| como | how | Como você está? (How are you?) |
| por que | why | Por que você estuda? (Why do you study?) |
| qual/quais | which/which ones | Qual é seu carro? (Which is your car?) |
| quanto/a/os/as | how much/many | Quantos filhos você tem? (How many children do you have?) |

**Detailed Usage:**

**O QUE / QUE (what):**
- O que você faz? (What do you do?)
- O que você fez ontem? (What did you do yesterday?)
- O que você vai fazer? (What are you going to do?)
- Que hora é? (What time is it?)
- Note: "que" is shorter, "o que" is more common in questions

**QUEM (who):**
- Quem é ele? (Who is he?)
- Quem mora aqui? (Who lives here?)
- Com quem você foi? (With whom did you go? / Who did you go with?)
- De quem é isso? (Whose is this? / literally: Of whom is this?)

**ONDE (where):**
- Onde você mora? (Where do you live?)
- Onde você trabalha? (Where do you work?)
- Onde você foi? (Where did you go?)
- Onde está meu livro? (Where is my book?)

**QUANDO (when):**
- Quando você vai viajar? (When are you going to travel?)
- Quando você chegou? (When did you arrive?)
- Quando é seu aniversário? (When is your birthday?)

**COMO (how):**
- Como você está? (How are you?)
- Como você vai ao trabalho? (How do you go to work?)
- Como se diz isso em português? (How do you say this in Portuguese?)
- Como é seu nome? (What's your name? / literally: How is your name?)

**POR QUE (why):**
- Por que você estuda português? (Why do you study Portuguese?)
- Por que você não foi? (Why didn't you go?)
- Por que você gosta disso? (Why do you like this?)

**QUAL / QUAIS (which / which ones):**
- Qual é seu nome? (What is your name?)
- Qual é sua profissão? (What is your profession?)
- Qual livro você gostou? (Which book did you like?)
- Quais são seus amigos? (Which ones are your friends?)

**QUANTO/A/OS/AS (how much / how many):**
- **Agreement with noun:**
  - Quanto custa? (How much does it cost?)
  - Quanta água? (How much water?)
  - Quantos irmãos? (How many brothers?)
  - Quantas irmãs? (How many sisters?)
- Quantos anos você tem? (How old are you? / literally: How many years do you have?)

**With All Three Tenses:**

**Present:**
- Onde você mora? (Where do you live?)
- O que você faz? (What do you do?)
- Quem é ele? (Who is he?)

**Future:**
- Quando você vai viajar? (When are you going to travel?)
- O que você vai fazer? (What are you going to do?)
- Onde você vai morar? (Where are you going to live?)

**Past:**
- Onde você morou? (Where did you live?)
- O que você fez? (What did you do?)
- Quando você foi? (When did you go?)
- Quem você viu? (Who did you see?)

**Sample Conversation:**
- A: Onde você mora? (Where do you live?)
- B: Moro em São Paulo. E você? (I live in São Paulo. And you?)
- A: Moro no Rio. Quando você foi a São Paulo? (I live in Rio. When did you go to São Paulo?)
- B: Fui há dois anos. Por que você pergunta? (I went two years ago. Why do you ask?)
- A: Porque vou viajar para lá. Qual bairro você mora? (Because I'm going to travel there. Which neighborhood do you live in?)

**Common Fixed Expressions:**
- Como vai? (How are you? / literally: How goes?)
- Como é que...? (How is it that...? - emphasis on the question)
- O que é isso? (What is this?)
- Quem sabe? (Who knows?)
- Onde fica...? (Where is... located?)
- Quanto tempo? (How long? / literally: How much time?)

**Question Word Order:**
- Simple: **Question word + verb + (subject)**
  - Onde mora você? (Where do you live?)
  - But more natural: Onde você mora? (Where do you live?)
- With pro-drop (no subject): **Question word + verb**
  - Onde mora? (Where do [you] live?)
  - Common in conversation

**Key Learning:**
- Students have encountered many of these informally (onde in Unit 3, como in Unit 21, etc.)
- Now systematizing all question words in one unit
- Can form questions in present, future, and past tenses
- Essential for conducting conversations, not just answering questions
- "quanto/a/os/as" shows gender/number agreement (like possessives)

**Why This Unit:**
- Natural progression: students have been answering questions, now they can ask them
- Systematizes question words encountered informally throughout Units 1-29
- Enables two-way conversation
- Ultra-granular: focusing only on interrogatives
- Immediately practical - students can now drive conversations
- Works with ALL tenses and ALL verbs learned so far
- **MAJOR MILESTONE**: Students can now conduct complete conversations in three tenses!

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- Unit 3: "Onde você mora?" - onde was used informally
- Unit 18: "onde, como, o que" mentioned
- Unit 29: "O que você fez?" introduced informally
- Unit 30: Now making all interrogatives systematic and explicit

---

### Unit 39: Reflexive Verbs (me chamo, me levanto, me sinto)
**New vocabulary:**
- **Reflexive pronouns:**
  - **me** (myself)
  - **se** (yourself/himself/herself/themselves)
  - **nos** (ourselves)
- **Common reflexive verbs:**
  - chamar-se (to call oneself / to be named)
  - levantar-se (to get up)
  - sentar-se (to sit down)
  - sentir-se (to feel)
  - vestir-se (to get dressed)
  - deitar-se (to lie down / go to bed)
  - lembrar-se (to remember)
  - esquecer-se (to forget)
- **Daily routine vocabulary:**
  - de manhã (in the morning)
  - à tarde (in the afternoon)
  - à noite (at night)
  - cedo (early)
  - tarde (late)
  - bem (well)
  - mal (badly)
  - cansado/a (tired)
  - feliz (happy)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Reflexive verbs: action reflects back on the subject**
- **Reflexive pronouns in Brazilian Portuguese go BEFORE the conjugated verb**
- Pattern: subject + reflexive pronoun + conjugated verb
  - Eu **me** chamo Maria (I call myself Maria = My name is Maria)
  - Eu **me** levanto cedo (I get up early)
  - Eu **me** sinto bem (I feel well)
- Reflexive pronouns for each subject:
  - eu → **me** (myself)
  - você/ele/ela → **se** (yourself/himself/herself)
  - nós → **nos** (ourselves)
  - vocês/eles/elas → **se** (yourselves/themselves)
- Common use: **"Como você se chama?"** = "What's your name?" (literally: How do you call yourself?)
- Answer: **"Me chamo [name]"** or informal **"Meu nome é [name]"** (Unit 13)

**Practice format:**
- "Me chamo João" (My name is João / I call myself João)
- "Me levanto às 6h" (I get up at 6am)
- "Me sinto bem hoje" (I feel well today)
- "Como você se chama?" (What's your name?)
- "Me visto rápido" (I get dressed quickly)

**Student can now:**
- Introduce themselves formally: "Me chamo [name]"
- Talk about daily routine (getting up, sitting down, going to bed)
- Express how they feel (me sinto bem/mal/cansado/feliz)
- Use reflexive verbs in all three tenses (present, future, past)
- Understand difference between reflexive and non-reflexive verbs
- Ask someone's name formally: "Como você se chama?"

**Typical sentences:**
- Me chamo Maria (My name is Maria)
- Me levanto às 7h (I get up at 7am)
- Me sinto bem (I feel well)
- Me sinto cansado (I feel tired)
- Não me sinto bem (I don't feel well)
- Me visto rápido de manhã (I get dressed quickly in the morning)
- Me sento aqui (I sit here)
- Me deito tarde (I go to bed late)
- Você se lembra? (Do you remember?)
- Não me lembro (I don't remember)
- Como você se chama? (What's your name?)

**Full Conjugation - Reflexive Verbs (Present Tense):**
| Pronoun | Reflexive Pronoun | chamar-se | levantar-se | sentir-se |
|---------|-------------------|-----------|-------------|-----------|
| eu | me | me chamo | me levanto | me sinto |
| você/ele/ela | se | se chama | se levanta | se sente |
| nós | nos | nos chamamos | nos levantamos | nos sentimos |
| vocês/eles/elas | se | se chamam | se levantam | se sentem |

**Examples with All Pronouns:**
- Eu me chamo João (My name is João)
- Você se chama Maria? (Is your name Maria?)
- Ele se levanta cedo (He gets up early)
- Ela se sente feliz (She feels happy)
- Nós nos sentamos aqui (We sit here)
- Vocês se lembram? (Do you all remember?)
- Eles se vestem rápido (They get dressed quickly)

**Reflexive vs Non-Reflexive:**
Some verbs can be used both ways:

| Non-Reflexive | Reflexive |
|---------------|-----------|
| Chamo meu amigo (I call my friend) | Me chamo João (I'm called João) |
| Levanto a mão (I raise my hand) | Me levanto cedo (I get up early) |
| Sinto frio (I feel cold - external) | Me sinto bem (I feel well - internal state) |
| Visto meu filho (I dress my son) | Me visto (I get dressed) |
| Sento o bebê (I sit the baby down) | Me sento (I sit down) |

**With All Three Tenses:**

**Present:**
- Me levanto cedo (I get up early)
- Me sinto bem (I feel well)
- Como você se chama? (What's your name?)

**Future (vou + infinitive):**
- Vou me levantar cedo amanhã (I'm going to get up early tomorrow)
- Vou me sentir melhor depois (I'm going to feel better later)
- Ela vai se vestir agora (She's going to get dressed now)
- Note: Pronoun can go before "vou" OR after the infinitive in BP
  - Me vou levantar (less common in BP)
  - Vou me levantar (common in BP)
  - Vou levantar-me (European Portuguese style, rare in BP)

**Past:**
- Me levantei cedo ontem (I got up early yesterday)
- Me senti bem (I felt well)
- Ele se vestiu rápido (He got dressed quickly)
- Nos sentamos lá (We sat there)

**Past Tense Conjugations:**
| Pronoun | chamar-se | levantar-se | sentir-se |
|---------|-----------|-------------|-----------|
| eu | me chamei | me levantei | me senti |
| você/ele/ela | se chamou | se levantou | se sentiu |
| nós | nos chamamos | nos levantamos | nos sentimos |
| vocês/eles/elas | se chamaram | se levantaram | se sentiram |

**Sample Conversation:**
- A: Como você se chama? (What's your name?)
- B: Me chamo Ana. E você? (My name is Ana. And you?)
- A: Me chamo Carlos. A que horas você se levanta? (My name is Carlos. What time do you get up?)
- B: Me levanto às 6h. E você? (I get up at 6am. And you?)
- A: Eu me levanto às 7h. Como você se sente hoje? (I get up at 7am. How do you feel today?)
- B: Me sinto bem, obrigada. (I feel well, thank you.)

**Common Daily Routine with Reflexive Verbs:**
- Me levanto às 6h (I get up at 6am)
- Me visto rápido (I get dressed quickly)
- Trabalho de manhã (I work in the morning - not reflexive)
- Me sinto cansado à tarde (I feel tired in the afternoon)
- Me deito às 10h (I go to bed at 10pm)

**With Negation:**
- Não me levanto cedo (I don't get up early)
- Não me sinto bem (I don't feel well)
- Ele não se lembra (He doesn't remember)
- Não me esqueci (I didn't forget)
- Ela não se vestiu ainda (She hasn't gotten dressed yet)

**"Me chamo" vs "Meu nome é":**
Both mean "My name is":
- **Me chamo João** - formal, using reflexive verb (literally: I call myself João)
- **Meu nome é João** (Unit 13) - informal, more common in conversation (My name is João)
- Both are correct and commonly used
- "Como você se chama?" is the formal question form
- "Qual é seu nome?" is also common (What is your name?)

**CRITICAL: Common Mistakes - Verbs That Are NOT Reflexive:**

⚠️ **FORBIDDEN - DO NOT use these verbs reflexively:**
- ❌ **"me acordo"** (WRONG) - acordar (to wake up) is NOT reflexive in Portuguese
- ❌ **"me durmo"** (WRONG) - dormir (to sleep) is NOT reflexive
- ❌ **"me desperto"** (WRONG) - despertar (to wake) is NOT reflexive
- ❌ **"me abro"** (WRONG) - abrir (to open) is NOT reflexive
- ❌ **"me fecho"** (WRONG) - fechar (to close) is NOT reflexive

✅ **CORRECT usage:**
- **Acordo às 7h** (I wake up at 7am) - NO pronoun
- **Durmo cedo** (I sleep early) - NO pronoun
- **Abro a porta** (I open the door) - NO pronoun

**Why this confusion?** These verbs seem personal ("I wake myself up"), but Portuguese treats them as non-reflexive. Only use the approved reflexive verbs list above!

**Three Types of Usage:**

**1. Reflexive (action on oneself):**
- Eu **me** levanto (I get myself up)
- Eu **me** visto (I dress myself)
- Ela **se** senta (She sits herself down)

**2. Reciprocal (action on each other - plural subjects only):**
- Nós **nos** vemos todo dia (We see each other every day)
- Eles **se** amam (They love each other)
- Vocês **se** conhecem? (Do you all know each other?)
- **Note:** Reciprocal meaning requires PLURAL subjects (nós, vocês, eles/elas)
- me/te are ALWAYS reflexive only (singular subjects can't be reciprocal)

**3. Non-Reflexive (same verb without pronoun - action on something/someone else):**
- **Reflexive:** Eu **me** lavo (I wash myself)
- **Non-Reflexive:** Eu lavo o carro (I wash the car - NO pronoun!)

- **Reflexive:** Eu **me** levanto às 7h (I get up at 7am)
- **Non-Reflexive:** Eu levanto pesos (I lift weights - NO pronoun!)

- **Reflexive:** Ela **se** veste (She dresses herself)
- **Non-Reflexive:** Ela veste o bebê (She dresses the baby - NO pronoun!)

- **Reflexive:** Eu **me** preparo (I prepare myself)
- **Non-Reflexive:** Eu preparo o jantar (I prepare dinner - NO pronoun!)

**Key Learning:**
- Reflexive verbs are essential for daily routine vocabulary
- Reflexive pronouns go BEFORE the verb in Brazilian Portuguese (not after like European Portuguese)
- "Me chamo" is the formal way to introduce yourself
- Many verbs can be used both reflexively and non-reflexively with different meanings
- Works naturally with all three tenses learned so far
- The pronoun must match the subject (eu → me, você → se, nós → nos)

**Why This Unit:**
- Natural progression after interrogatives - students can now ask "Como você se chama?"
- Essential for daily routine conversations
- Introduces new pronoun category (reflexive) while building on existing pronoun knowledge
- Ultra-granular: focusing only on reflexive verbs, not other pronoun types
- Immediate practical value - "me chamo" and "me sinto" are used constantly
- Builds foundation for object pronouns in future units
- **MILESTONE**: Students can now introduce themselves formally!

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- Unit 13: "Meu nome é João" (informal name introduction)
- Unit 31: "Me chamo João" (formal name introduction with reflexive verb)
- Unit 18: "Como" used informally
- Unit 31: "Como você se chama?" (systematic formal question)
- Unit 1-23: Regular verbs learned
- Unit 31: Same verbs can be used reflexively (levantar → levantar-se)

---

### Unit 40: Direct Object Pronouns (me, te, o/a, nos, os/as)
**New vocabulary:**
- **Direct object pronouns:**
  - **me** (me - as object)
  - **te** (you - as object, informal)
  - **o / a** (him/it / her/it - masculine/feminine)
  - **nos** (us - as object)
  - **os / as** (them - masculine/feminine plural)
- **New verbs commonly used with direct objects:**
  - ver (to see - already learned in Unit 33)
  - conhecer (to know/meet - people/places)
  - amar (to love)
  - ajudar (to help)
  - esperar (to wait for / to hope)
  - ouvir (to hear/listen)
  - entender (to understand)
  - encontrar (to find / to meet)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Direct object pronouns: replace the direct object (the thing/person receiving the action)**
- **In Brazilian Portuguese, pronouns typically go BEFORE the verb (like reflexive pronouns)**
- Pattern: subject + object pronoun + verb
  - Ele **me** vê (He sees me)
  - Eu **te** amo (I love you)
  - Eu **o** conheço (I know him)
  - Ela **nos** ajuda (She helps us)
- Direct object answers "what?" or "whom?"
  - Vejo João → Vejo quem? João → **O** vejo (I see him)
  - Amo Maria → Amo quem? Maria → **A** amo (I love her)
  - Conhecemos as pessoas → **As** conhecemos (We know them)
- Gender and number agreement with o/a/os/as
  - **o** = him/it (masculine singular)
  - **a** = her/it (feminine singular)
  - **os** = them (masculine plural or mixed)
  - **as** = them (feminine plural)

**Practice format:**
- "Ele me vê" (He sees me)
- "Te amo" (I love you)
- "Conheço-o bem" → "O conheço bem" (I know him well)
- "Ela nos ajuda" (She helps us)
- "Vejo-os todos os dias" → "Os vejo todos os dias" (I see them every day)

**Student can now:**
- Replace direct objects with pronouns to sound more natural
- Avoid repetition: "Vejo João. João é meu amigo." → "Vejo João. O conheço bem."
- Use object pronouns with all three tenses
- Distinguish between reflexive pronouns (Unit 35) and direct object pronouns (Unit 36)
- Understand that me/nos can be reflexive OR object pronouns (context determines)
- Form more natural, fluent Portuguese sentences

**Typical sentences:**
- Ele me vê todos os dias (He sees me every day)
- Te amo (I love you)
- O conheço bem (I know him well)
- A vejo na escola (I see her at school)
- Ela nos ajuda (She helps us)
- Vocês os conhecem? (Do you all know them?)
- Não as vejo mais (I don't see them anymore - feminine)
- Me entendem? (Do you understand me?)
- Te espero aqui (I wait for you here / I'll wait for you here)

**Direct Object Pronouns:**
| Pronoun | Meaning | Example |
|---------|---------|---------|
| me | me | Ele me vê (He sees me) |
| te | you (informal) | Te amo (I love you) |
| o | him/it (masc) | O conheço (I know him) |
| a | her/it (fem) | A vejo (I see her) |
| nos | us | Ela nos ajuda (She helps us) |
| os | them (masc/mixed) | Os conheço (I know them) |
| as | them (fem) | As vejo (I see them) |

**Examples with Different Verbs:**

**Ver (to see):**
- Ele me vê (He sees me)
- Te vejo amanhã (I see you tomorrow / I'll see you tomorrow)
- O vejo todos os dias (I see him every day)
- Nos veem na escola (They see us at school)

**Conhecer (to know):**
- Você me conhece? (Do you know me?)
- Te conheço de onde? (Where do I know you from?)
- O conheço bem (I know him well)
- Não a conheço (I don't know her)
- Nos conhecemos há anos (We've known each other for years - reflexive usage)

**Amar (to love):**
- Te amo (I love you)
- O amo muito (I love him very much)
- Ela nos ama (She loves us)

**Ajudar (to help):**
- Você me ajuda? (Can you help me? / Do you help me?)
- Te ajudo sempre (I always help you)
- Ela os ajuda (She helps them)

**Entender (to understand):**
- Você me entende? (Do you understand me?)
- Te entendo perfeitamente (I understand you perfectly)
- Não o entendo (I don't understand him)

**Comparing Reflexive (Unit 35) vs Direct Object (Unit 36):**

| Reflexive (action on self) | Direct Object (action on other) |
|----------------------------|----------------------------------|
| Me levanto (I get myself up) | Ele me levanta (He picks me up) |
| Me visto (I dress myself) | Ela me veste (She dresses me) |
| Me chamo João (I call myself João) | Ele me chama (He calls me) |
| Nos sentamos (We sit ourselves) | Eles nos sentam (They sit us down - rare) |

**Note:** me/nos can be EITHER reflexive OR direct object - context determines:
- **Me levanto** cedo (reflexive - I get myself up)
- Ele **me** vê (direct object - he sees me)
- **Nos** sentimos bem (reflexive - we feel well)
- Ela **nos** ajuda (direct object - she helps us)

**With All Three Tenses:**

**Present:**
- Me vê todos os dias (He sees me every day)
- Te amo (I love you)
- O conheço (I know him)
- Nos ajudam (They help us)

**Future (vou + infinitive):**
- Vou te ver amanhã (I'm going to see you tomorrow)
- Ele vai me ajudar (He's going to help me)
- Vamos conhecê-los (We're going to meet them)
- Note: In BP, pronoun typically goes before main verb, but can attach to infinitive

**Past:**
- Me viu ontem (He saw me yesterday)
- Te amei (I loved you)
- O conheci na escola (I met him at school)
- Nos ajudaram muito (They helped us a lot)
- Não as vi (I didn't see them)

**Position in Brazilian Portuguese:**
- **Standard (most common):** Pronoun BEFORE verb
  - Me vê (He sees me)
  - Te amo (I love you)
  - O conheço (I know him)

- **After infinitive (less common but correct):**
  - Quero vê-lo (I want to see him)
  - Vou conhecê-la (I'm going to meet her)
  - Note: Hyphen connects pronoun to verb

- **European Portuguese often puts pronoun after:** "Vejo-o" (I see him)
- **Brazilian Portuguese prefers pronoun before:** "O vejo" (I see him)

**Gender and Number Agreement with o/a/os/as:**
Must match the noun being replaced:

- João (masculine singular) → **o** → O conheço
- Maria (feminine singular) → **a** → A conheço
- Os meninos (masculine plural) → **os** → Os conheço
- As meninas (feminine plural) → **as** → As conheço
- Mixed group (João e Maria) → **os** → Os conheço (masculine plural for mixed)

**Sample Conversation:**
- A: Você conhece João? (Do you know João?)
- B: Sim, o conheço bem. Ele é meu amigo. (Yes, I know him well. He's my friend.)
- A: Quando você o viu? (When did you see him?)
- B: O vi ontem. Ele me ajudou com o trabalho. (I saw him yesterday. He helped me with work.)
- A: E Maria? Você a conhece também? (And Maria? Do you know her too?)
- B: Sim, a conheço. Vou vê-la amanhã. (Yes, I know her. I'm going to see her tomorrow.)

**With Negation:**
- Não me vê (He doesn't see me)
- Não te amo (I don't love you)
- Não o conheço (I don't know him)
- Não nos ajudam (They don't help us)
- Nunca os vejo (I never see them)

**CRITICAL: Standard vs Colloquial Brazilian Portuguese**

This unit teaches **standard/formal BP** with clitic pronouns (me, te, o/a, nos, os/as) placed BEFORE the verb. However, you MUST know that **colloquial spoken BP** is very different:

**Standard/Formal BP (taught in this unit):**
- ✅ **Eu o vi** (I saw him) - clitic pronoun before verb
- ✅ **Eu a conheço** (I know her) - clitic pronoun before verb
- ✅ **Eu os encontrei** (I found them) - clitic pronoun before verb

**Colloquial/Spoken BP (VERY common in daily speech):**
- ✅ **Eu vi ele** (I saw him) - stressed pronoun after verb, VERY COMMON
- ✅ **Eu conheço ela** (I know her) - stressed pronoun after verb, VERY COMMON
- ✅ **Eu encontrei eles** (I found them) - stressed pronoun after verb, VERY COMMON
- ✅ **Vejo você** (I see you) - stressed pronoun after verb, VERY COMMON

**Which should you use?**
- **Writing/formal contexts:** Use clitic pronouns (o/a/os/as) before the verb
- **Speaking/informal contexts:** Brazilians commonly use stressed pronouns (ele/ela/você) after the verb
- **Both are correct!** But colloquial forms dominate in everyday conversation

**About "TE" (you - informal):**
⚠️ **IMPORTANT:** "Te" is RARE in Brazilian Portuguese!
- ❌ **"Te amo"** - used in songs/poetry, but uncommon in daily speech
- ✅ **"Amo você"** - much more common in Brazilian Portuguese
- ✅ **"Te amo"** - common in European Portuguese (with "tu")

**Why is "te" rare in BP?**
- BP uses "você" (not "tu") as the standard "you"
- "Você" requires "o/a" pronouns, not "te"
- "Te" is associated with "tu" (uncommon in most of Brazil)

**Practical Recommendation for Students:**
1. **Learn the standard forms** (this unit) - needed for writing and formal speech
2. **Understand colloquial forms** (ele/ela after verb) - you'll hear these constantly
3. **Use "você" instead of "te"** in your own speech - more natural in BP

**Common Mistakes to Avoid:**
1. **Wrong agreement:** "O vejo" for Maria → Should be "**A** vejo" (feminine)
2. **Wrong position:** "Vejo-o" (European) → BP prefers "O vejo"
3. **Confusing reflexive and object:**
   - "Me levanto" (reflexive - I get up)
   - "Ele me levanta" (object - he lifts me up)
4. **Overusing "te" in BP:**
   - Less common: "Te vejo amanhã" (sounds formal/literary)
   - More common: "Vejo você amanhã" (natural BP)

**Practical Usage:**
Direct object pronouns make speech more natural and avoid repetition:

**Without pronouns (repetitive):**
- Conheço João. Vejo João todos os dias. Gosto de João.

**With pronouns (natural):**
- Conheço João. **O** vejo todos os dias. Gosto dele.

**Key Learning:**
- Direct object pronouns replace nouns to avoid repetition
- me/nos can be reflexive (Unit 35) OR direct object (Unit 36) - context determines
- o/a/os/as must agree in gender and number with the noun they replace
- Brazilian Portuguese puts pronouns BEFORE the verb (unlike European Portuguese)
- Works with all three tenses
- Makes speech sound more natural and fluent
- Essential for intermediate-level fluency

**Why This Unit:**
- Natural progression after reflexive pronouns (Unit 35)
- Both use similar forms (me, nos) but different functions
- Essential for fluent, natural-sounding Portuguese
- Reduces repetition in speech
- Ultra-granular: focusing only on direct object pronouns (indirect comes later)
- Immediate practical value - used constantly in conversation
- **MILESTONE**: Students can now form more sophisticated, natural sentences!

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- Unit 31: Reflexive pronouns (me chamo, me levanto)
- Unit 32: Direct object pronouns (me vê, me ajuda)
- Unit 29: Ver (to see) - now can use "o vejo" instead of "vejo ele"
- Unit 16: Gosto de (Unit 19 uses indirect object - "de + person")
- Unit 32: Direct object (no preposition) - "o vejo" not "vejo de ele"

**Important Distinction:**
- **Direct object (Unit 36):** NO preposition - "Vejo João" → "**O** vejo"
- **Indirect object (future unit):** WITH preposition - "Falo com João" (uses "lhe" or "para ele")

---

### Unit 41: Past Tense - More Common Irregular Verbs (poder, querer, saber)
**New vocabulary:**
- **Three more essential irregular verbs in preterite:**
  - poder (to be able to / can)
  - querer (to want)
  - saber (to know - facts/information)
- **Additional vocabulary:**
  - nada (nothing)
  - tudo (everything)
  - a verdade (the truth)
  - a resposta (the answer)
  - a notícia (the news)
  - comprar (to buy - regular verb for examples)
  - vir (to come - for context, but conjugation comes later)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Preterite tense for poder, querer, and saber**
- These three verbs often change meaning slightly in the past:
  - **poder** (present: can/am able to) → (past: could/was able to/managed to)
  - **querer** (present: want) → (past: wanted/tried to)
  - **saber** (present: know) → (past: found out/learned)
- Conjugation patterns:
  - **poder**: pude, pôde, pudemos, puderam
  - **querer**: quis, quis, quisemos, quiseram
  - **saber**: soube, soube, soubemos, souberam
- All three are highly irregular with unique stems

**Practice format:**
- "Pude ir ao trabalho" (I was able to go to work / I managed to go to work)
- "Quis comprar, mas não pude" (I wanted to buy, but couldn't)
- "Soube a verdade ontem" (I found out the truth yesterday)
- "Ele não quis falar" (He didn't want to speak / He refused to speak)

**Student can now:**
- Talk about what they could or couldn't do (pude/não pude)
- Express past desires and intentions (quis/não quis)
- Talk about finding out information (soube)
- Understand the nuanced meaning shifts in the past tense
- Combine with other past tense verbs for richer storytelling

**Typical sentences:**
- Pude ir (I was able to go / I managed to go)
- Não pude trabalhar ontem (I couldn't work yesterday)
- Quis viajar, mas não pude (I wanted to travel, but couldn't)
- Ele não quis comer (He didn't want to eat / He refused to eat)
- Soube a notícia hoje (I found out the news today)
- Quando você soube? (When did you find out?)
- Não soube a resposta (I didn't know the answer)
- Pudemos ver tudo (We were able to see everything)

**Full Conjugation - More Common Irregulars:**
| Pronoun | poder | querer | saber |
|---------|-------|--------|-------|
| eu | pude | quis | soube |
| você/ele/ela | pôde | quis | soube |
| nós | pudemos | quisemos | soubemos |
| vocês/eles/elas | puderam | quiseram | souberam |

**Pattern Recognition:**

**poder** (pude, pôde, pudemos, puderam):
- Stem changes from "pod-" to "pud-/pôd-"
- "pôde" has circumflex accent to distinguish from "pode" (present tense)
- Similar to "pôr" family of verbs (which we'll learn later)

**querer** (quis, quis, quisemos, quiseram):
- Stem changes from "quer-" to "quis-"
- eu/você forms identical: "quis"
- z sound throughout
- Very irregular pattern

**saber** (soube, soube, soubemos, souberam):
- Stem changes from "sab-" to "soub-"
- eu/você forms identical: "soube"
- Similar pattern to "ter" (tive, teve) but different vowel

**Comparing Present and Past:**
| Verb | Present (eu) | Past (eu) | Example |
|------|--------------|-----------|---------|
| poder | posso | pude | Posso ir → Pude ir |
| querer | quero | quis | Quero viajar → Quis viajar |
| saber | sei | soube | Sei a verdade → Soube a verdade |

**Meaning Shifts in Past Tense:**

**PODER (to be able to / can):**
- **Present:** ability or permission
  - Posso nadar (I can swim - I know how)
  - Posso ir? (Can I go? - permission)
- **Past:** managed to or tried and succeeded
  - Pude nadar (I was able to swim / I managed to swim - specific event)
  - Pude ir (I was able to go / I managed to go)
- **Negative past:** tried but failed
  - Não pude ir (I couldn't go / I wasn't able to go)

**QUERER (to want):**
- **Present:** current desire
  - Quero café (I want coffee)
- **Past:** wanted at that specific time, often implies attempt
  - Quis comprar café (I wanted to buy coffee - and tried)
- **Negative past:** refused or didn't want
  - Não quis falar (He didn't want to speak / He refused to speak)
  - Strong implication of choice/decision

**SABER (to know):**
- **Present:** knowledge you have now
  - Sei português (I know Portuguese)
  - Sei a resposta (I know the answer)
- **Past:** found out, learned, discovered
  - Soube a verdade (I found out the truth / I learned the truth)
  - Soube ontem (I found out yesterday)
- This is a KEY difference - "soube" = "found out" not just "knew"

**Common Uses for "poder" (past):**
- Pude ir ao trabalho (I was able to go to work)
- Não pude dormir (I couldn't sleep)
- Pude ver o filme (I was able to see the movie / I managed to see the movie)
- Por que você não pôde vir? (Why couldn't you come? / Why weren't you able to come?)
- Pudemos comprar a casa (We were able to buy the house)

**Common Uses for "querer" (past):**
- Quis falar com você (I wanted to talk to you)
- Não quis comer (I didn't want to eat / I refused to eat)
- Ele quis ajudar (He wanted to help)
- Quisemos viajar (We wanted to travel)
- Por que você não quis ir? (Why didn't you want to go?)
- Note: "não quis" often implies deliberate refusal

**Common Uses for "saber" (past):**
- Soube a notícia ontem (I found out the news yesterday)
- Quando você soube? (When did you find out?)
- Soube que ele foi ao Brasil (I found out that he went to Brazil)
- Não soube a resposta (I didn't know the answer - at that specific moment)
- Ela soube a verdade (She found out the truth)
- Como você soube? (How did you find out?)

**Sample Conversation:**
- A: Por que você não foi à festa? (Why didn't you go to the party?)
- B: Não pude ir. Tive que trabalhar. (I couldn't go. I had to work.)
- A: Mas você quis ir? (But did you want to go?)
- B: Sim, quis muito, mas não pude. (Yes, I really wanted to, but I couldn't.)
- A: Você soube que Maria foi? (Did you find out that Maria went?)
- B: Sim, soube hoje de manhã. (Yes, I found out this morning.)

**Combining with Previous Irregular Verbs:**

**Telling a story with multiple irregular verbs:**
- Quis ir ao cinema, mas não pude. (I wanted to go to the movies, but couldn't.)
- Tive que trabalhar. (I had to work.) [Unit 32]
- Fui ao trabalho cedo. (I went to work early.) [Unit 32]
- Fiz muito trabalho. (I did a lot of work.) [Unit 33]
- Depois, vi meus amigos. (Afterwards, I saw my friends.) [Unit 33]
- Soube que eles também quiseram ir ao cinema. (I found out they also wanted to go to the movies.)
- Não pudemos ir, mas estivemos juntos. (We couldn't go, but we were together.) [Unit 32]

**Common Combinations:**

**Poder + Infinitive:**
- Pude viajar (I was able to travel)
- Não pude ver (I couldn't see)
- Pudemos comprar (We were able to buy)

**Querer + Infinitive:**
- Quis estudar (I wanted to study)
- Não quis falar (I didn't want to speak / I refused to speak)
- Quisemos ajudar (We wanted to help)

**Saber + Noun:**
- Soube a verdade (I found out the truth)
- Soube a notícia (I found out the news)
- Não soube nada (I didn't know anything / I didn't find out anything)

**Saber + Que-clause:**
- Soube que ele foi (I found out that he went)
- Soube que ela está bem (I found out that she's well)

**With Negation:**
- Não pude ir (I couldn't go)
- Não quis falar (I didn't want to speak / I refused to speak)
- Não soube nada (I didn't find out anything)
- Ele não pôde vir (He couldn't come)
- Ela não quis comer (She didn't want to eat)
- Não soubemos a verdade (We didn't find out the truth)

**Expressing "I tried but couldn't":**
- Quis comprar, mas não pude (I wanted to buy, but couldn't)
- Quis ir, mas não pude (I wanted to go, but couldn't)
- Quisemos ajudar, mas não pudemos (We wanted to help, but couldn't)
- This combination is VERY common in conversation
