- Practical: immediate use for describing routine, habits, schedule
- Enriches descriptions of daily life significantly

---

### Unit 64: Food and Meals Expanded (Comida e Refeições - Expandido)

**New vocabulary:**
- **Proteins:**
  - a carne (meat)
  - o frango (chicken)
  - o peixe (fish)
  - o ovo (egg)
  - o queijo (cheese)

- **Vegetables:**
  - a alface (lettuce)
  - o tomate (tomato)
  - a cenoura (carrot)
  - a batata (potato)
  - a cebola (onion)

- **Fruits:**
  - a maçã (apple)
  - a banana (banana)
  - a laranja (orange)
  - o morango (strawberry)
  - a uva (grape)

- **Staples:**
  - o arroz (rice)
  - o feijão (beans)
  - o pão (bread)
  - a massa (pasta)
  - o açúcar (sugar)
  - o sal (salt)

- **Drinks:**
  - a água (water)
  - o suco (juice)
  - o refrigerante (soda)
  - o leite (milk)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Using food with verbs:**
  - **comer** (to eat) + food: "Eu como arroz" (I eat rice)
  - **beber** (to drink) + beverage: "Eu bebo água" (I drink water)
  - **gostar de** (to like) + food: "Eu gosto de frango" (I like chicken)

- **Gender surprises in food vocabulary:**
  - **o tomate** (tomato - masculine, even though ends in -e)
  - **o leite** (milk - masculine)
  - **a carne** (meat - feminine)
  - **o sal** (salt - masculine)
  - Gender is not predictable - must memorize!

- **Partitives and quantities:**
  - um pedaço de pão (a piece of bread)
  - um copo de água (a glass of water)
  - uma xícara de café (a cup of coffee)
  - um prato de arroz (a plate of rice)
  - um pouco de sal (a little salt)

- **Brazilian staple: Arroz e feijão**
  - "Arroz **com** feijão" (rice and beans) - use COM (with)
  - This is THE staple of Brazilian cuisine, eaten daily
  - Often said as one phrase: "arroz e feijão"

**Practice format:**
- Name foods with correct gender/article
- Use gostar de + food: "Eu gosto de banana"
- Order meals: "Eu quero frango com arroz"
- Describe what you eat: "Eu como ovos no café da manhã"
- Practice quantities: "um copo de suco"

**Student can now:**
- Name 28 common foods and drinks
- Use correct gender for food vocabulary
- Express food preferences with gostar de
- Order food and describe meals
- Use basic quantity expressions

**Typical sentences:**
- Eu gosto de arroz e feijão. (I like rice and beans.)
- Eu como frango com batata. (I eat chicken with potato.)
- Eu bebo suco de laranja. (I drink orange juice.)
- Eu quero um pedaço de pão. (I want a piece of bread.)
- Ela não come carne. (She doesn't eat meat.)
- Eu como frutas todos os dias. (I eat fruit every day.)
- Eu bebo água, não refrigerante. (I drink water, not soda.)

**Sample conversation:**
```
A: O que você gosta de comer?
   (What do you like to eat?)
B: Eu gosto de frango com arroz e feijão.
   (I like chicken with rice and beans.)

A: Você come carne?
   (Do you eat meat?)
B: Sim, eu como. Mas eu prefiro frango.
   (Yes, I do. But I prefer chicken.)

A: E o que você bebe?
   (And what do you drink?)
B: Eu bebo água e às vezes suco.
   (I drink water and sometimes juice.)

A: Você gosta de frutas?
   (Do you like fruit?)
B: Sim, muito! Eu gosto de banana e morango.
   (Yes, a lot! I like banana and strawberry.)
```

**Common Mistakes to Avoid:**
- ❌ "Eu gosto frango" (missing "de")
- ✅ "Eu gosto de frango" (correct - gostar requires "de")
- ❌ "a tomate" (wrong gender)
- ✅ "o tomate" (correct - masculine)
- ❌ "Arroz com feijões" (wrong - feijão stays singular in this phrase)
- ✅ "Arroz com feijão" (correct - Brazilian staple phrase)
- ❌ "Eu bebo um suco de o laranja" (wrong - must contract)
- ✅ "Eu bebo um suco de laranja" (correct)

**Brazilian Food Culture:**
- **Arroz e feijão** is the foundation of Brazilian meals
- Eaten at lunch (main meal) almost daily
- Usually accompanied by protein (chicken, beef, fish) and salad
- Breakfast (café da manhã): bread, coffee, fruit, cheese
- Lunch (almoço): main meal, rice and beans with protein
- Dinner (jantar): lighter, or leftovers from lunch

**Gender Patterns (and exceptions):**
Most foods ending in -a are feminine, -o masculine, BUT:
- **o tomate** (masculine exception)
- **o leite** (masculine)
- **a carne** (feminine)
- **o peixe** (masculine)
- Must memorize gender for each food!

**Quantity Expressions:**
- **um pedaço de** (a piece of): um pedaço de bolo (a piece of cake)
- **um copo de** (a glass of): um copo de leite (a glass of milk)
- **uma xícara de** (a cup of): uma xícara de café (a cup of coffee)
- **um prato de** (a plate of): um prato de arroz (a plate of rice)
- **um pouco de** (a little of): um pouco de açúcar (a little sugar)
- **muito/muita** (a lot of): muita água (a lot of water), muito arroz (a lot of rice)

**Food Preferences:**
- Eu gosto de... (I like...)
- Eu prefiro... (I prefer...)
- Eu adoro... (I love...)
- Eu não gosto de... (I don't like...)
- Eu odeio... (I hate...)
- Eu amo... (I love...)

**Dietary Restrictions (for recognition):**
- vegetariano/vegetariana (vegetarian)
- vegano/vegana (vegan)
- Eu não como carne. (I don't eat meat.)
- Eu sou alérgico a... (I'm allergic to...)
- sem glúten (gluten-free)
- sem lactose (lactose-free)

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- Unit 25: Gostar de → "Eu gosto de arroz"
- Unit 20-19: Basic food → now expanding vocabulary significantly
- Unit 61: Meals → "Eu como ovos no café da manhã"
- Unit 62: Frequency → "Eu como frutas todos os dias"
- Unit 15: Negation → "Eu não como carne"

**Key Learning:**
- 28 essential food and drink vocabulary items
- ARROZ COM FEIJÃO is Brazilian staple (rice and beans)
- Gender must be memorized (o tomate, a carne, o leite)
- Gostar de + food for preferences (requires "de")
- Essential for ordering food, describing diet, social situations

**Why This Unit:**
- **FOUNDATIONAL:** Food is universal conversation topic
- Natural progression: expanding basic food vocabulary from earlier units
- Ultra-granular: focuses ONLY on food vocabulary and usage
- Practical: immediate use for eating out, shopping, describing habits
- Culturally relevant: introduces Brazilian food culture (arroz e feijão)

---

### Unit 65: Transportation and Travel (Transporte e Viagem)

**New vocabulary:**
- **Modes of transportation:**
  - o carro (car)
  - o ônibus (bus)
  - o metrô (subway/metro)
  - o trem (train)
  - o avião (airplane)
  - o táxi (taxi)
  - o Uber (Uber)
  - a bicicleta (bicycle)
  - a moto (motorcycle)
  - o barco (boat)
  - a pé (on foot)

- **Travel vocabulary:**
  - a viagem (trip/travel)
  - o aeroporto (airport)
  - a estação (station)
  - o bilhete (ticket)
  - a passagem (ticket - for travel)
  - a mala (suitcase)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Transportation prepositions - DE vs A PÉ:**
  - **de** + vehicle: "Eu vou **de** carro" (I go by car)
  - **de** ônibus, de metrô, de táxi, de avião, de trem, de bicicleta
  - **Exception: a pé** (on foot): "Eu vou **a pé**" (I go on foot)
  - NOT "de pé" - this is an exception!

- **IR (to go) + means of transportation:**
  - Eu vou de ônibus. (I go by bus.)
  - Eu vou de carro. (I go by car.)
  - Ele vai a pé. (He goes on foot.)
  - Structure: IR + de + transportation

- **PEGAR (to take/catch) + vehicle:**
  - Eu pego o ônibus. (I take/catch the bus.)
  - Eu pego o metrô. (I take the subway.)
  - "Pegar" means "to take/catch/get" a vehicle
  - Use definite article: pego **o** ônibus (not "pego ônibus")

- **Travel expressions with PARA:**
  - Eu vou **para** São Paulo. (I'm going to São Paulo.)
  - Eu viajo **para** o Brasil. (I'm traveling to Brazil.)
  - Use PARA (to/toward) for destination

**Practice format:**
- Name transportation with correct articles
- Practice "de + vehicle": "Eu vou de ônibus"
- Use pegar + vehicle: "Eu pego o metrô"
- Describe travel: "Eu viajo para São Paulo de avião"
- Ask/answer transportation questions

**Student can now:**
- Name 11 modes of transportation
- Use correct preposition (de) with vehicles
- Use "a pé" correctly for walking
- Express how they get places: "Eu vou de carro"
- Talk about travel plans and destinations

**Typical sentences:**
- Eu vou de ônibus. (I go by bus.)
- Eu vou para o trabalho de carro. (I go to work by car.)
- Ela vai a pé. (She goes on foot.)
- Eu pego o metrô todos os dias. (I take the subway every day.)
- Eu viajo de avião. (I travel by plane.)
- Eu vou para São Paulo amanhã. (I'm going to São Paulo tomorrow.)
- Quanto custa a passagem de ônibus? (How much does the bus ticket cost?)

**Sample conversation:**
```
A: Como você vai para o trabalho?
   (How do you go to work?)
B: Eu vou de metrô. É rápido.
   (I go by subway. It's fast.)

A: Quanto tempo leva?
   (How much time does it take?)
B: Leva 30 minutos.
   (It takes 30 minutes.)

A: E no fim de semana, como você se move?
   (And on weekends, how do you get around?)
B: Eu geralmente vou de carro ou a pé.
   (I usually go by car or on foot.)

A: Você vai viajar nas férias?
   (Are you going to travel on vacation?)
B: Sim, eu vou para a praia de ônibus.
   (Yes, I'm going to the beach by bus.)
```

**Common Mistakes to Avoid:**
- ❌ "Eu vou em carro" (wrong preposition)
- ✅ "Eu vou de carro" (correct - use "de")
- ❌ "Eu vou de pé" (wrong - common mistake!)
- ✅ "Eu vou a pé" (correct - exception to the rule)
- ❌ "Eu pego ônibus" (missing article)
- ✅ "Eu pego o ônibus" (correct - need article with pegar)
- ❌ "Eu vou para o trabalho em metrô" (wrong preposition)
- ✅ "Eu vou para o trabalho de metrô" (correct)

**Transportation Preposition Rule:**

**Use DE with all vehicles:**
- de carro (by car)
- de ônibus (by bus)
- de metrô (by subway)
- de táxi (by taxi)
- de Uber (by Uber)
- de avião (by plane)
- de trem (by train)
- de bicicleta (by bicycle)
- de moto (by motorcycle)
- de barco (by boat)

**EXCEPTION - Use A PÉ:**
- a pé (on foot) - NOT "de pé"!

**PEGAR (to take/catch) - Irregular verb:**
Present tense:
- eu pego (I take)
- você pega (you take)
- ele/ela pega (he/she takes)
- nós pegamos (we take)
- vocês pegam (you all take)
- eles/elas pegam (they take)

Common uses:
- pegar o ônibus (take the bus)
- pegar o metrô (take the subway)
- pegar um táxi (catch a taxi)
- pegar o trem (catch the train)

**Brazilian Transportation Context:**
- **Ônibus** is the most common public transport in most cities
- **Metrô** exists in major cities (São Paulo, Rio, Brasília, etc.)
- **Uber** is very popular and common in Brazil
- Many people go **a pé** in city centers
- Traffic (trânsito) can be very heavy in big cities

**Distance and Time:**
- longe (far): "O trabalho é longe." (Work is far.)
- perto (near): "A escola é perto." (The school is near.)
- Quanto tempo leva? (How long does it take?)
- Leva 30 minutos. (It takes 30 minutes.)

**Asking About Transportation:**
- Como você vai para...? (How do you get to...?)
- Quanto tempo leva? (How long does it take?)
- Quanto custa? (How much does it cost?)
- Onde eu pego o ônibus? (Where do I catch the bus?)
- Que ônibus vai para...? (Which bus goes to...?)

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- Unit 7: Places → "Eu vou para o trabalho de carro"
- Unit 26: Future (IR + infinitive) → using IR for destinations
- Unit 59: Directions → combining with transportation
- Unit 62: Frequency → "Eu pego o metrô todos os dias"
- Unit 48: Time → "Leva 30 minutos"

**Key Learning:**
- 11 modes of transportation vocabulary
- Use DE with all vehicles (de carro, de ônibus, de avião)
- Exception: A PÉ (on foot) - not "de pé"!
- PEGAR + article + vehicle (pego o ônibus)
- Essential for daily life, describing routine, travel

**Why This Unit:**
- **FOUNDATIONAL:** Transportation is essential daily vocabulary
- Natural progression: can describe daily activities, now how you get there
- Ultra-granular: focuses ONLY on transportation and travel
- Practical: immediate use for navigation, describing routine, travel plans
- Addresses common mistake: "a pé" vs "de + vehicle"

---

### Unit 66: Hobbies and Leisure Activities (Hobbies e Atividades de Lazer)

**New vocabulary:**
- **Sports and activities:**
  - jogar futebol (to play soccer)
  - jogar vôlei (to play volleyball)
  - jogar basquete (to play basketball)
  - nadar (to swim)
  - correr (to run)
  - caminhar (to walk/hike)
  - dançar (to dance)
  - cantar (to sing)

- **Leisure activities:**
  - ler (to read)
  - escrever (to write)
  - desenhar (to draw)
  - pintar (to paint)
  - tocar (to play instrument)
  - ouvir música (to listen to music)
  - assistir TV (to watch TV)
  - assistir filmes (to watch movies)
  - jogar videogame (to play video games)
  - viajar (to travel)
  - cozinhar (to cook)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **JOGAR vs TOCAR - Critical distinction:**
  - **JOGAR** = play SPORTS/GAMES
    - jogar futebol (play soccer)
    - jogar vôlei (play volleyball)
    - jogar videogame (play video games)
    - jogar cartas (play cards)
  - **TOCAR** = play MUSICAL INSTRUMENTS
    - tocar violão (play guitar)
    - tocar piano (play piano)
    - tocar bateria (play drums)
  - **Do NOT confuse these two!**

- **GOSTAR DE + infinitive (to like to...):**
  - Eu gosto de ler. (I like to read.)
  - Ela gosta de nadar. (She likes to swim.)
  - Structure: gostar de + infinitive verb

- **Frequency with hobbies:**
  - Combining frequency adverbs (Unit 63) with hobbies:
  - Eu **sempre** jogo futebol. (I always play soccer.)
  - Eu **às vezes** leio. (I sometimes read.)

- **No article with sports after JOGAR:**
  - ✅ Eu jogo futebol. (I play soccer.) - NO article
  - ❌ Eu jogo o futebol. (wrong - don't use article)
  - Exception: specific game/match uses article
  - "Eu vou jogar o jogo" (I'm going to play the game - specific)

**Practice format:**
- Name hobbies and activities
- Use gostar de + infinitive: "Eu gosto de nadar"
- Practice JOGAR vs TOCAR distinction
- Describe hobbies with frequency: "Eu sempre leio"
- Ask about others' hobbies

**Student can now:**
- Name 19 common hobbies and leisure activities
- Use JOGAR correctly for sports/games
- Use TOCAR correctly for instruments
- Express hobby preferences: "Eu gosto de ler"
- Combine hobbies with frequency adverbs

**Typical sentences:**
- Eu jogo futebol todo sábado. (I play soccer every Saturday.)
- Eu gosto de ler livros. (I like to read books.)
- Ela toca piano. (She plays piano.)
- Eu gosto de assistir filmes. (I like to watch movies.)
- Nós jogamos vôlei na praia. (We play volleyball on the beach.)
- Eu corro todos os dias. (I run every day.)
- Eu ouço música quando estudo. (I listen to music when I study.)

**Sample conversation:**
```
A: O que você gosta de fazer no tempo livre?
   (What do you like to do in your free time?)
B: Eu gosto de jogar futebol e ler.
   (I like to play soccer and read.)

A: Você joga futebol com que frequência?
   (How often do you play soccer?)
B: Eu jogo todo sábado com meus amigos.
   (I play every Saturday with my friends.)

A: Você toca algum instrumento?
   (Do you play any instrument?)
B: Sim, eu toco violão.
   (Yes, I play guitar.)

A: E o que você lê?
   (And what do you read?)
B: Eu leio romances e livros de história.
   (I read novels and history books.)
```

**Common Mistakes to Avoid:**
- ❌ "Eu toco futebol" (wrong - sports use JOGAR)
- ✅ "Eu jogo futebol" (correct)
- ❌ "Eu jogo violão" (wrong - instruments use TOCAR)
- ✅ "Eu toco violão" (correct)
- ❌ "Eu jogo o futebol" (wrong - no article with sports)
- ✅ "Eu jogo futebol" (correct)
- ❌ "Eu gosto nadar" (missing "de")
- ✅ "Eu gosto de nadar" (correct - gostar requires "de")

**JOGAR vs TOCAR - Complete Guide:**

**Use JOGAR for:**
- **Sports:** futebol, vôlei, basquete, tênis
- **Games:** videogame, cartas, xadrez (chess)
- **General "play" meaning:** jogar bola (play ball)

Examples:
- Eu jogo futebol. (I play soccer.)
- Ele joga videogame. (He plays video games.)
- Nós jogamos cartas. (We play cards.)

**Use TOCAR for:**
- **Musical instruments:** violão, piano, bateria, guitarra
- **Literally means "to touch"** but used for instruments

Examples:
- Eu toco piano. (I play piano.)
- Ela toca violão. (She plays guitar.)
- Eles tocam bateria. (They play drums.)

**No Article with Sports:**
When using JOGAR with sports, NO article is needed:
- ✅ jogar futebol (play soccer)
- ✅ jogar tênis (play tennis)
- ✅ jogar basquete (play basketball)
- ❌ jogar o futebol (wrong - no article)

**UNLESS referring to a specific game:**
- Vou jogar **o jogo** amanhã. (I'm going to play the game tomorrow.)
- Assistimos **o jogo** ontem. (We watched the game yesterday.)

**Musical Instruments:**
Common instruments in Portuguese:
- o violão (acoustic guitar)
- a guitarra (electric guitar)
- o piano (piano)
- a bateria (drums)
- o baixo (bass)
- a flauta (flute)
- o violino (violin)

**Brazilian Sports Culture:**
- **Futebol** (soccer) is THE national sport
- Almost everyone plays or watches futebol
- Beach volleyball (vôlei de praia) is very popular
- Capoeira is a Brazilian martial art/dance
- Surfing is popular in coastal areas

**Asking About Hobbies:**
- O que você gosta de fazer no tempo livre? (What do you like to do in your free time?)
- Quais são seus hobbies? (What are your hobbies?)
- Você pratica algum esporte? (Do you practice any sport?)
- Você toca algum instrumento? (Do you play any instrument?)

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- Unit 25: Gostar de → "Eu gosto de ler"
- Unit 62: Frequency → "Eu jogo futebol todo sábado"
- Unit 49: Days → "Eu jogo vôlei na sexta"
- Unit 61: Activities → expanding activity vocabulary
- Unit 64: Food → "Eu gosto de cozinhar"

**Key Learning:**
- 19 hobby and leisure activity verbs
- JOGAR for sports/games, TOCAR for instruments - CRITICAL distinction
- No article with sports: "jogar futebol" (not "jogar o futebol")
- Gostar de + infinitive for preferences: "gosto de ler"
- Essential for social conversation, describing interests

**Why This Unit:**
- **FOUNDATIONAL:** Hobbies are essential social conversation
- Natural progression: can describe daily activities, now leisure time
- Ultra-granular: focuses ONLY on hobbies and leisure
- Practical: immediate use for socializing, making friends, conversation
- Addresses critical JOGAR vs TOCAR distinction

---

### Unit 67: Technology and Communication (Tecnologia e Comunicação)

**New vocabulary:**
- **Devices:**
  - o celular (cell phone)
  - o telefone (telephone)
  - o computador (computer)
  - o notebook (laptop)
  - o tablet (tablet)
  - a televisão / TV (television)
  - o relógio (watch/clock)

- **Communication:**
  - ligar (to call)
  - mandar mensagem (to send message)
  - enviar (to send)
  - receber (to receive)
  - responder (to respond/reply)
  - a mensagem (message)
  - o email (email)
  - o WhatsApp (WhatsApp)

- **Internet:**
  - a internet (internet)
  - o site (website)
  - o WiFi (WiFi)
  - a senha (password)
  - baixar (to download)
  - postar (to post)
  - o app / aplicativo (app)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Technology vocabulary often borrowed from English:**
  - WhatsApp, email, WiFi, site, app - same as English!
  - Pronounced with Portuguese accent but spelled similarly
  - Many tech terms are international

- **LIGAR (to call) - Multiple meanings:**
  - **ligar para** + person: "Eu ligo **para** você" (I call you)
  - **ligar** + device: "Eu ligo o computador" (I turn on the computer)
  - Same verb, different meanings based on context!
  - Use PARA when calling a person

- **MANDAR vs ENVIAR (both mean "to send"):**
  - **mandar** is more casual/common: "Eu mando uma mensagem"
  - **enviar** is more formal: "Eu envio um email"
  - Both are correct, mandar is more conversational

- **Using technology verbs:**
  - Eu **uso** o celular. (I use the cell phone.)
  - Eu **ligo** para minha mãe. (I call my mother.)
  - Eu **mando** mensagem. (I send a message.)
  - Eu **baixo** apps. (I download apps.)

**Practice format:**
- Name devices with correct articles
- Practice "ligar para" + person
- Use communication verbs: mandar, enviar, receber
- Describe technology use: "Eu uso o celular para..."
- Ask about WiFi, passwords, etc.

**Student can now:**
- Name 21 technology and communication terms
- Use LIGAR correctly (for calling and turning on)
- Use communication verbs (mandar, enviar, receber)
- Talk about technology use and habits
- Ask for WiFi password, phone numbers, etc.

**Typical sentences:**
- Eu uso o celular todos os dias. (I use my cell phone every day.)
- Eu ligo para minha família toda semana. (I call my family every week.)
- Eu mando mensagem no WhatsApp. (I send messages on WhatsApp.)
- Você tem WiFi? (Do you have WiFi?)
- Qual é a senha do WiFi? (What's the WiFi password?)
- Eu envio emails para o trabalho. (I send emails for work.)
- Eu baixo muitos apps. (I download many apps.)

**Sample conversation:**
```
A: Você usa muito o celular?
   (Do you use your cell phone a lot?)
B: Sim, eu uso o dia todo.
   (Yes, I use it all day.)

A: Para que você usa?
   (What do you use it for?)
B: Eu mando mensagens, ligo para meus amigos, e navego na internet.
   (I send messages, call my friends, and browse the internet.)

A: Você tem WhatsApp?
   (Do you have WhatsApp?)
B: Sim, todo mundo no Brasil usa WhatsApp.
   (Yes, everyone in Brazil uses WhatsApp.)

A: Qual é seu número?
   (What's your number?)
B: É 11 9-1234-5678.
   (It's 11 9-1234-5678.)
```

**Common Mistakes to Avoid:**
- ❌ "Eu ligo você" (missing preposition)
- ✅ "Eu ligo para você" (correct - need "para")
- ❌ "a WiFi" (wrong gender)
- ✅ "o WiFi" (correct - masculine)
- ❌ "Eu mando mensagem para WhatsApp" (awkward)
- ✅ "Eu mando mensagem no WhatsApp" (correct - use "no")
- ❌ "o internet" (wrong gender)
- ✅ "a internet" (correct - feminine)

**LIGAR - Two Main Meanings:**

**Meaning 1: To CALL (phone):**
- Structure: ligar **para** + person
- Eu ligo **para** você. (I call you.)
- Eu ligo **para** minha mãe. (I call my mother.)
- Você pode ligar **para** mim? (Can you call me?)

**Meaning 2: To TURN ON (device):**
- Structure: ligar + device (no preposition)
- Eu ligo o computador. (I turn on the computer.)
- Eu ligo a TV. (I turn on the TV.)
- Eu ligo o carro. (I start the car.)

**Opposite: DESLIGAR (to turn off, to hang up):**
- Eu desligo o celular. (I turn off the cell phone.)
- Eu desligo a chamada. (I hang up the call.)

**Brazilian Tech Culture:**
- **WhatsApp is DOMINANT** in Brazil - everyone uses it
- More popular than SMS or other messaging apps
- Used for personal and business communication
- Common to ask "Tem WhatsApp?" (Do you have WhatsApp?)
- Video calls: "chamada de vídeo" or "videochamada"

**Phone Number Format in Brazil:**
- **Format:** (XX) 9XXXX-XXXX
- **Area code** (código de área): (11) for São Paulo, (21) for Rio
- **Mobile numbers** start with 9
- Example: (11) 9-1234-5678

**Asking for Contact Information:**
- Qual é seu número? (What's your number?)
- Você tem WhatsApp? (Do you have WhatsApp?)
- Qual é seu email? (What's your email?)
- Qual é a senha do WiFi? (What's the WiFi password?)
- Você tem internet? (Do you have internet?)

**Technology Verbs:**
- **usar** (to use): Eu uso o computador.
- **ligar** (to call/turn on): Eu ligo para você.
- **desligar** (to turn off/hang up): Eu desligo o celular.
- **mandar** (to send): Eu mando mensagem.
- **enviar** (to send): Eu envio email.
- **receber** (to receive): Eu recebo mensagens.
- **responder** (to reply): Eu respondo rápido.
- **baixar** (to download): Eu baixo apps.
- **postar** (to post): Eu posto fotos.

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- Unit 63: Frequency → "Eu uso o celular todos os dias"
- Unit 62: Daily activities → technology is part of routine
- Unit 38: Questions → "Qual é a senha?" (What's the password?)
- Unit 58: Family → "Eu ligo para minha mãe"

**Key Learning:**
- 21 technology and communication vocabulary terms
- LIGAR PARA + person (to call), LIGAR + device (to turn on)
- WhatsApp is dominant messaging platform in Brazil
- Many tech terms borrowed from English (email, WiFi, app)
- Essential for modern communication and daily life

**Why This Unit:**
- **FOUNDATIONAL:** Technology is essential in modern life
- Natural progression: can communicate, now describe tech tools
- Ultra-granular: focuses ONLY on technology and communication
- Practical: immediate use for daily life, staying in touch, navigation
- Culturally relevant: WhatsApp dominance in Brazil

---

### Unit 68: Shopping and Money (Compras e Dinheiro)

**New vocabulary:**
- **Money:**
  - o dinheiro (money)
  - o real (Brazilian currency - singular)
  - os reais (Brazilian currency - plural)
  - a moeda (coin)
  - a nota (bill/banknote)
  - o cartão (card)
  - o cartão de crédito (credit card)
  - o cartão de débito (debit card)
  - o Pix (instant payment system)
  - o troco (change)

- **Shopping:**
  - a loja (store)
  - o mercado (market)
  - o supermercado (supermarket)
  - a farmácia (pharmacy)
  - comprar (to buy)
  - vender (to sell)
  - custar (to cost)
  - pagar (to pay)
  - o preço (price)
  - barato (cheap)
  - caro (expensive)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Brazilian currency: REAL/REAIS**
  - **Singular:** um real (R$ 1,00)
  - **Plural:** dois reais, três reais, cem reais
  - Written: R$ (símbolo do real)
  - R$ 10,00 = dez reais

- **CUSTAR (to cost) - special verb:**
  - **3rd person only** (like DOER in Unit 57)
  - Subject is the thing that costs, not the person!
  - **Singular:** custa (it costs)
  - **Plural:** custam (they cost)
  - Examples:
    - Quanto **custa**? (How much does it cost?)
    - **Custa** dez reais. (It costs ten reais.)
    - Os livros **custam** vinte reais. (The books cost twenty reais.)

- **PAGAR (to pay) - takes direct object OR por:**
  - Eu pago dez reais. (I pay ten reais.) - direct object
  - Eu pago **pelo** livro. (I pay for the book.) - por + o = pelo
  - Both structures are correct

- **PIX - Brazilian instant payment:**
  - Revolutionary payment system in Brazil (launched 2020)
  - Instant bank-to-bank transfer via phone
  - "Você aceita Pix?" (Do you accept Pix?)
  - "Eu faço um Pix" (I'll make a Pix payment)
  - Has largely replaced cash in Brazil!

**Practice format:**
- Name money vocabulary with correct articles
- Practice prices: "Custa dez reais"
- Use shopping verbs: comprar, vender, pagar
- Ask "Quanto custa?" (How much does it cost?)
- Describe payment methods: "Eu pago com cartão"

**Student can now:**
- Name 21 shopping and money terms
- Use CUSTAR correctly (3rd person only)
- Ask and understand prices in reais
- Talk about payment methods (Pix, card, cash)
- Describe shopping experiences

**Typical sentences:**
- Quanto custa? (How much does it cost?)
- Custa dez reais. (It costs ten reais.)
- Eu pago com cartão. (I pay with card.)
- Você aceita Pix? (Do you accept Pix?)
- Isso é muito caro. (This is very expensive.)
- Eu compro no supermercado. (I buy at the supermarket.)
- Eu preciso de troco. (I need change.)

**Sample conversation:**
```
A: Quanto custa este livro?
   (How much does this book cost?)
B: Custa vinte e cinco reais.
   (It costs twenty-five reais.)

A: É um pouco caro. Você tem mais barato?
   (It's a bit expensive. Do you have cheaper?)
B: Sim, esse aqui custa quinze reais.
   (Yes, this one costs fifteen reais.)

A: Ótimo! Eu levo. Você aceita Pix?
   (Great! I'll take it. Do you accept Pix?)
B: Sim, aceitamos Pix, cartão, e dinheiro.
   (Yes, we accept Pix, card, and cash.)
```

**Common Mistakes to Avoid:**
- ❌ "Quanto eu custo?" (wrong - YOU don't cost, things cost)
- ✅ "Quanto custa?" (correct - thing is subject)
- ❌ "Custa dois real" (missing plural)
- ✅ "Custa dois reais" (correct - plural)
- ❌ "dez real" (wrong - use plural)
- ✅ "dez reais" (correct)
- ❌ "Eu pago por cartão" (awkward)
- ✅ "Eu pago com cartão" (correct - use "com")

**CUSTAR (to cost) - Special Verb:**

Like DOER (to hurt), CUSTAR uses 3rd person only:
- **Singular:** custa (one thing costs)
  - O livro custa dez reais. (The book costs ten reais.)
  - Quanto custa? (How much does it cost?)

- **Plural:** custam (multiple things cost)
  - Os livros custam vinte reais. (The books cost twenty reais.)
  - Quanto custam? (How much do they cost?)

**The thing that costs is the SUBJECT**, not the person buying!

**Brazilian Currency: REAL (R$)**
- **Singular:** um real (1 real)
- **Plural:** reais (multiple reais)
- **Symbol:** R$
- **Written format:** R$ 10,00 (ten reais)
- **Decimal:** comma (,) not period
  - R$ 10,50 = dez reais e cinquenta centavos
  - Period (.) separates thousands: R$ 1.000,00 (one thousand reais)

**Money denominations:**
- **Coins (moedas):** 5, 10, 25, 50 centavos, 1 real
- **Bills (notas):** R$ 2, 5, 10, 20, 50, 100, 200

**PIX - Brazilian Payment Revolution:**
- **Launched 2020** by Brazilian Central Bank
- **Instant transfers** between any banks
- **Use:** phone number, email, CPF, or QR code
- **Free for individuals**
- **Dominant payment method** in Brazil now
- "Fazer um Pix" (to make a Pix payment)
- "Mandar um Pix" (to send a Pix)
- Has revolutionized Brazilian economy!

**Payment Methods:**
- **dinheiro** (cash): Eu pago em dinheiro.
- **cartão de crédito** (credit card): Eu pago com cartão de crédito.
- **cartão de débito** (debit card): Eu pago com débito.
- **Pix** (instant payment): Eu faço um Pix. / Eu pago com Pix.

**Shopping Vocabulary:**
- **comprar** (to buy): Eu compro pão.
- **vender** (to sell): Eles vendem frutas.
- **custar** (to cost): Custa dez reais.
- **pagar** (to pay): Eu pago com Pix.

**Asking About Price:**
- Quanto custa? (How much does it cost?)
- Qual é o preço? (What's the price?)
- Quanto é? (How much is it?)
- Tem desconto? (Is there a discount?)

**Describing Price:**
- **caro** (expensive): Isso é muito caro.
- **barato** (cheap): Isso é barato.
- **em conta** (affordable): É bem em conta.
- **bom preço** (good price): É um bom preço.

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- Unit 15-16: Numbers → prices in reais
- Unit 38: Questions → "Quanto custa?"
- Unit 64: Food → "Eu compro comida no supermercado"
- Unit 61: Places → "loja", "mercado", "farmácia"
- Unit 19: Precisar de → "Eu preciso de troco"

**Key Learning:**
- 21 shopping and money vocabulary terms
- CUSTAR is 3rd person only (custa/custam) - thing is subject
- Brazilian currency: real (singular), reais (plural)
- PIX is dominant payment method in Brazil (revolutionary!)
- Essential for shopping, transactions, daily life

**Why This Unit:**
- **FOUNDATIONAL:** Money and shopping are essential daily activities
- Natural progression: can name things, now buy them
- Ultra-granular: focuses ONLY on shopping and money
- Practical: immediate use for any purchase, transaction
- Culturally relevant: introduces PIX (uniquely Brazilian innovation)

---

### Unit 69: Professions and Work (Profissões e Trabalho)

**New vocabulary:**
- **Common professions:**
  - o médico / a médica (doctor)
  - o professor / a professora (teacher)
  - o enfermeiro / a enfermeira (nurse)
  - o engenheiro / a engenheira (engineer)
  - o advogado / a advogada (lawyer)
  - o dentista / a dentista (dentist - same form!)
  - o jornalista / a jornalista (journalist - same form!)
  - o estudante / a estudante (student - same form!)
  - o cozinheiro / a cozinheira (cook/chef)
  - o garçom / a garçonete (waiter/waitress)
  - o vendedor / a vendedora (salesperson)
  - o empresário / a empresária (businessperson)
  - o artista / a artista (artist - same form!)
  - o policial / a policial (police officer - same form!)

- **Work vocabulary:**
  - o trabalho (work/job)
  - a empresa (company)
  - o escritório (office)
  - o chefe / a chefe (boss)
  - o colega / a colega (colleague - same form!)
  - o salário (salary)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Gender agreement in professions:**
  - Most professions change -o to -a for feminine:
    - médico → médica
    - professor → professora
    - cozinheiro → cozinheira

  - Professions ending in -ista, -nte stay the SAME:
    - o dentista / a dentista (same word!)
    - o estudante / a estudante (same word!)
    - o artista / a artista (same word!)
    - Only the article changes!

- **Professions with unique feminine forms:**
  - o garçom / a garçonete (waiter/waitress - completely different)
  - o ator / a atriz (actor/actress - different forms)

- **Talking about professions - Two structures:**

  **Structure 1: SER + profession (no article):**
  - Eu sou médico. (I am a doctor.)
  - Ela é professora. (She is a teacher.)
  - NO article needed in Portuguese!

  **Structure 2: TRABALHAR COMO (work as):**
  - Eu trabalho como médico. (I work as a doctor.)
  - Ela trabalha como professora. (She works as a teacher.)

- **TRABALHAR EM (work at) vs TRABALHAR COMO (work as):**
  - **EM** = location: "Eu trabalho **em** um hospital" (I work at a hospital)
  - **COMO** = profession: "Eu trabalho **como** médico" (I work as a doctor)
  - Can combine: "Eu trabalho como médico em um hospital"

**Practice format:**
- Name professions with correct gender forms
- Practice "sou + profession" (no article)
- Use "trabalhar como" for professions
- Use "trabalhar em" for locations
- Describe what family members do

**Student can now:**
- Name 20+ common professions with correct gender
- Use SER + profession correctly (without article)
- Distinguish trabalhar EM (location) vs COMO (profession)
- Ask and answer about occupations
- Describe workplace and colleagues

**Typical sentences:**
- Eu sou professor. (I am a teacher.)
- Ela é médica. (She is a doctor.)
- Eu trabalho como engenheiro. (I work as an engineer.)
- Eu trabalho em um hospital. (I work at a hospital.)
- Meu pai é advogado. (My father is a lawyer.)
- Ela trabalha como jornalista em São Paulo. (She works as a journalist in São Paulo.)
- O que você faz? - Eu sou dentista. (What do you do? - I'm a dentist.)

**Sample conversation:**
```
A: O que você faz?
   (What do you do?)
B: Eu sou professor. E você?
   (I'm a teacher. And you?)

A: Eu trabalho como enfermeira.
   (I work as a nurse.)
B: Onde você trabalha?
   (Where do you work?)

A: Eu trabalho em um hospital no centro.
   (I work at a hospital downtown.)
B: Você gosta do seu trabalho?
   (Do you like your job?)

A: Sim, muito! É cansativo, mas eu gosto.
   (Yes, a lot! It's tiring, but I like it.)
```

**Common Mistakes to Avoid:**
- ❌ "Eu sou um médico" (wrong - no article needed)
- ✅ "Eu sou médico" (correct - no article)
- ❌ "Ela é um professora" (wrong - no article + wrong article)
- ✅ "Ela é professora" (correct)
- ❌ "Eu trabalho como em hospital" (wrong - mixing structures)
- ✅ "Eu trabalho em um hospital" (correct)
- ❌ "o dentisto" / "a dentisto" (wrong - doesn't change)
- ✅ "o dentista" / "a dentista" (correct - same form)

**SER + Profession - NO ARTICLE:**

This is a MAJOR difference from English:
- **English:** I am **a** doctor. (uses article)
- **Portuguese:** Eu sou médico. (NO article)

Examples:
- Eu sou professor. (I am a teacher.)
- Ela é engenheira. (She is an engineer.)
- Eles são estudantes. (They are students.)
- Nós somos advogados. (We are lawyers.)

**Exception:** When you add an adjective, USE article:
- Eu sou **um bom** médico. (I am a good doctor.)
- Ela é **uma** professora **excelente**. (She is an excellent teacher.)

**Professions That DON'T Change Form:**

These professions use the SAME word for masculine and feminine:
- **-ista endings:**
  - o/a dentista (dentist)
  - o/a jornalista (journalist)
  - o/a artista (artist)
  - o/a pianista (pianist)

- **-nte endings:**
  - o/a estudante (student)
  - o/a assistente (assistant)
  - o/a gerente (manager)

- **-al endings:**
  - o/a policial (police officer)

**Only the ARTICLE changes:**
- o dentista (male dentist)
- a dentista (female dentist)

**TRABALHAR - Three Structures:**

**1. TRABALHAR (alone) = to work:**
- Eu trabalho muito. (I work a lot.)
- Ela trabalha de segunda a sexta. (She works Monday to Friday.)

**2. TRABALHAR EM = work at/in (location):**
- Eu trabalho **em** uma empresa. (I work at a company.)
- Ela trabalha **em** São Paulo. (She works in São Paulo.)

**3. TRABALHAR COMO = work as (profession):**
- Eu trabalho **como** professor. (I work as a teacher.)
- Ele trabalha **como** vendedor. (He works as a salesperson.)

**Combining:**
- Eu trabalho **como** médica **em** um hospital. (I work as a doctor at a hospital.)

**Asking About Professions:**
- O que você faz? (What do you do?)
- Qual é sua profissão? (What is your profession?)
- Você trabalha com o quê? (What do you work with?)
- Onde você trabalha? (Where do you work?)
- Em que você trabalha? (What do you work in?)

**Brazilian Work Culture:**
- Standard work week: Monday-Friday (segunda a sexta)
- Work hours often 9am-6pm (nove às dezoito)
- Lunch break: usually 1-2 hours
- "CLT" (Consolidação das Leis do Trabalho) = formal employment contract
- Many people work informally ("trabalho informal")

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- Unit 1: SER → "Eu sou professor"
- Unit 5: TRABALHAR → now expanding with professions
- Unit 9: Places → "Eu trabalho em São Paulo"
- Unit 58: Family → "Meu pai é advogado"
- Unit 38: Questions → "O que você faz?"

**Key Learning:**
- 20+ common professions with correct gender forms
- SER + profession WITHOUT article (major difference from English)
- Trabalhar EM (location) vs Trabalhar COMO (profession)
- Professions ending in -ista/-nte/-al don't change form
- Essential for introductions, describing self and others

**Why This Unit:**
- **FOUNDATIONAL:** Profession is one of first things people ask
- Natural progression: can describe activities, now describe occupation
- Ultra-granular: focuses ONLY on professions and work
- Practical: immediate use for introductions, networking, conversation
- Addresses common mistake: article with professions

---

### Unit 70: Health and Medical Basics (Saúde e Médico)

**New vocabulary:**
- **Health conditions:**
  - doente (sick)
  - saudável (healthy)
  - a febre (fever)
  - a tosse (cough)
  - o resfriado (cold/flu)
  - a gripe (flu)
  - a dor (pain)
  - o remédio (medicine)
  - o comprimido (pill)
  - a receita (prescription)

- **Medical places:**
  - o hospital (hospital)
  - a clínica (clinic)
  - o consultório (doctor's office)
  - o posto de saúde (health center)
  - a farmácia (pharmacy)

- **Medical professionals (review + expand):**
  - o médico / a médica (doctor)
  - o enfermeiro / a enfermeira (nurse)
  - o dentista / a dentista (dentist)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **ESTAR doente (to be sick) - uses ESTAR:**
  - Eu **estou** doente. (I am sick - temporary condition)
  - NOT "sou doente" - that would mean permanently sick!
  - Temporary health states always use ESTAR

- **TER (to have) with illnesses:**
  - Eu **tenho** febre. (I have a fever.)
  - Eu **tenho** tosse. (I have a cough.)
  - Eu **tenho** gripe. (I have the flu.)
  - Use TER (not ESTAR) for specific symptoms/illnesses

- **ESTAR COM (to be with) - alternative structure:**
  - Eu **estou com** febre. (I am with fever = I have a fever.)
  - Eu **estou com** dor de cabeça. (I have a headache.)
  - Both TER and ESTAR COM are correct!

- **Illness expressions:**
  - estar doente (to be sick)
  - estar bem (to be well)
  - estar mal (to feel bad/unwell)
  - ficar doente (to get/become sick)
  - melhorar (to get better)
  - piorar (to get worse)

**Practice format:**
- Describe symptoms: "Eu tenho febre"
- Use ESTAR for general sick state: "Estou doente"
- Practice TER vs ESTAR COM for symptoms
- Ask how someone is: "Como você está?"
- Describe at doctor: "Eu tenho dor de..."

**Student can now:**
- Describe common health problems and symptoms
- Use ESTAR correctly for being sick
- Use TER for specific illnesses/symptoms
- Name medical places and professionals
- Ask for medicine and describe problems to doctor

**Typical sentences:**
- Eu estou doente. (I am sick.)
- Eu tenho febre. (I have a fever.)
- Eu estou com dor de cabeça. (I have a headache.)
- Eu preciso de um médico. (I need a doctor.)
- Eu vou à farmácia. (I'm going to the pharmacy.)
- Ela está com gripe. (She has the flu.)
- Eu preciso de remédio. (I need medicine.)

**Sample conversation:**
```
A: Como você está?
   (How are you?)
B: Não estou bem. Estou doente.
   (I'm not well. I'm sick.)

A: O que você tem?
   (What's wrong? / What do you have?)
B: Eu tenho febre e dor de cabeça.
   (I have a fever and headache.)

A: Você foi ao médico?
   (Did you go to the doctor?)
B: Não, eu vou hoje.
   (No, I'm going today.)

A: Melhoras!
   (Get well! / Feel better!)
B: Obrigado!
   (Thank you!)
```

**Common Mistakes to Avoid:**
- ❌ "Eu sou doente" (wrong - implies permanently sick)
- ✅ "Eu estou doente" (correct - temporary state)
- ❌ "Eu estou febre" (wrong - febre is noun, needs TER)
- ✅ "Eu tenho febre" (correct)
- ❌ "Eu tenho doente" (wrong - doente is adjective, needs ESTAR)
- ✅ "Eu estou doente" (correct)

**ESTAR vs SER with Health:**

**Use ESTAR for temporary health states:**
- Eu **estou** doente. (I am sick - temporary)
- Eu **estou** bem. (I am well - temporary state)
- Eu **estou** mal. (I feel bad - temporary)

**SER would imply permanent condition:**
- Eu **sou** saudável. (I am healthy - generally, as a trait)
- But NOT "Eu sou doente" (sounds like chronic/permanent illness)

**TER vs ESTAR COM - Both Correct:**

**Use TER (more direct):**
- Eu **tenho** febre. (I have a fever.)
- Eu **tenho** tosse. (I have a cough.)
- Eu **tenho** gripe. (I have the flu.)
- Eu **tenho** dor. (I have pain.)

**Use ESTAR COM (more descriptive):**
- Eu **estou com** febre. (I am with fever = I have a fever.)
- Eu **estou com** tosse. (I have a cough.)
- Eu **estou com** gripe. (I have the flu.)
- Eu **estou com** dor. (I have pain.)

Both structures mean the same thing! Choose either.

**Common Illness Expressions:**
Building on Unit 57 (body parts):
- dor de cabeça (headache)
- dor de barriga (stomachache)
- dor de garganta (sore throat)
- dor de dente (toothache)
- dor nas costas (back pain)
- dor no peito (chest pain)

Structure: dor + de/em/no/na + body part

**Describing Symptoms to Doctor:**
- Eu tenho... (I have...)
- Eu sinto... (I feel...)
- Minha cabeça dói. (My head hurts.)
- Eu não estou bem. (I'm not well.)
- Desde quando? (Since when?)
- Há dois dias. (For two days.)

**At the Pharmacy:**
- Eu preciso de remédio para... (I need medicine for...)
- Tem algo para dor de cabeça? (Do you have something for headache?)
- Precisa de receita? (Does it need a prescription?)
- Quanto custa? (How much does it cost?)

**Brazilian Healthcare System:**
- **SUS** (Sistema Único de Saúde) = public healthcare (free)
- **Plano de saúde** = private health insurance
- **Posto de saúde** = public health center (neighborhood clinics)
- **Farmácia** = pharmacy (very accessible, many on every street)
- Some medicines available over-the-counter (sem receita)

**Getting Better:**
- melhorar (to get better): "Eu estou melhorando." (I'm getting better.)
- piorar (to get worse): "Eu estou piorando." (I'm getting worse.)
- recuperar (to recover): "Eu me recuperei." (I recovered.)
- curar (to cure/heal): "O remédio me curou." (The medicine cured me.)

**Well Wishes:**
- Melhoras! (Get well!)
- Fique bem! (Get well! / Be well!)
- Espero que você melhore logo! (I hope you get better soon!)
- Cuide-se! (Take care!)

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- Unit 56: Body parts → "dor de cabeça", "dor nas costas"
- Unit 58: Feelings → "Como você está?" "Eu estou mal"
- Unit 5: ESTAR → "Eu estou doente"
- Unit 16: TER → "Eu tenho febre"
- Unit 69: Professions → "médico", "enfermeiro"

**Key Learning:**
- Health vocabulary: doente, febre, tosse, resfriado, gripe, remédio
- ESTAR doente (temporary sick state) - NOT "sou doente"
- TER or ESTAR COM for symptoms (both correct)
- Medical places: hospital, clínica, consultório, farmácia
- Essential for describing health problems, getting help

**Why This Unit:**
- **FOUNDATIONAL:** Health vocabulary is critical for safety
- Natural progression: have body parts (56), now describe problems
- Ultra-granular: focuses ONLY on basic health vocabulary
- Practical: immediate use for doctor visits, pharmacy, emergencies
- Safety: essential vocabulary for travelers and residents

---

### Unit 71: Commands/Imperative Mood (Imperativo)

**New vocabulary:**
- **Common command verbs:**
  - falar (to speak) → Fale! (Speak!)
  - comer (to eat) → Coma! (Eat!)
  - abrir (to open) → Abra! (Open!)
  - fechar (to close) → Feche! (Close!)
  - esperar (to wait) → Espere! (Wait!)
  - vir (to come) → Venha! (Come!)
  - ir (to go) → Vá! (Go!)
  - fazer (to do) → Faça! (Do!)
  - sentar (to sit) → Sente-se! (Sit down!)
  - levantar (to get up) → Levante-se! (Get up!)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Imperative mood - Commands:**
  - Used to give orders, instructions, requests
  - Different forms for você, vocês, and nós
  - This unit focuses on **você** form (most common)

- **Forming você commands:**

  **For -AR verbs:** Change -a to -e
  - falar → você fala → **Fale!** (Speak!)
  - comprar → você compra → **Compre!** (Buy!)
  - fechar → você fecha → **Feche!** (Close!)

  **For -ER/-IR verbs:** Change -e to -a
  - comer → você come → **Coma!** (Eat!)
  - abrir → você abre → **Abra!** (Open!)
  - escrever → você escreve → **Escreva!** (Write!)

- **Pattern: Flip the present tense vowel!**
  - -AR verbs: -a → -e
  - -ER/-IR verbs: -e → -a

- **Negative commands:**
  - Add **NÃO** before the verb:
  - **Não fale!** (Don't speak!)
  - **Não coma!** (Don't eat!)
  - **Não abra!** (Don't open!)

- **Common irregular imperatives:**
  - **ir** → **Vá!** (Go!)
  - **vir** → **Venha!** (Come!)
  - **fazer** → **Faça!** (Do!)
  - **ser** → **Seja!** (Be!)
  - **ter** → **Tenha!** (Have!)
  - **dar** → **Dê!** (Give!)
  - **estar** → **Esteja!** (Be!)

**Practice format:**
- Form commands from regular verbs: falar → Fale!
- Practice irregular commands: ir → Vá!
- Use negative commands: Não fale!
- Give instructions: "Abra o livro"
- Polite requests with "por favor"

**Student can now:**
- Give direct commands in Portuguese
- Form regular imperative (flip vowel rule)
- Use common irregular imperatives
- Make negative commands (não + imperative)
- Give polite instructions with "por favor"

**Typical sentences:**
- Fale português! (Speak Portuguese!)
- Coma devagar! (Eat slowly!)
- Venha aqui! (Come here!)
- Vá para casa! (Go home!)
- Não fale alto! (Don't speak loudly!)
- Abra a porta, por favor. (Open the door, please.)
- Espere um momento! (Wait a moment!)

**Sample conversation:**
```
Professor: Abram os livros na página 10.
           (Open the books to page 10.)
           [Note: Abram = vocês form, but you'll learn that later]

Student: Qual página?
         (Which page?)

Professor: Página 10. Agora leiam o texto.
           (Page 10. Now read the text.)

Student: Em voz alta?
         (Out loud?)

Professor: Não, leiam em silêncio.
           (No, read silently.)
```

**Common Mistakes to Avoid:**
- ❌ "Fala português!" (wrong - that's present tense, not command)
- ✅ "Fale português!" (correct - imperative form)
- ❌ "Come isso!" (wrong - present tense)
- ✅ "Coma isso!" (correct - imperative)
- ❌ "Vai aqui!" (wrong - present tense)
- ✅ "Vá aqui!" or better "Venha aqui!" (correct - imperative)

**Imperative Formation - The Vowel Flip:**

**Regular -AR verbs (change -a to -e):**
- falar → você fal**a** → Fal**e**! (Speak!)
- comprar → você compr**a** → Compr**e**! (Buy!)
- estudar → você estud**a** → Estud**e**! (Study!)
- trabalhar → você trabalh**a** → Trabalh**e**! (Work!)

**Regular -ER/-IR verbs (change -e to -a):**
- comer → você com**e** → Com**a**! (Eat!)
- beber → você beb**e** → Beb**a**! (Drink!)
- abrir → você abr**e** → Abr**a**! (Open!)
- escrever → você escrev**e** → Escrev**a**! (Write!)

**Memory trick:** The vowel "flips" from the present tense você form!

**Common Irregular Imperatives:**

These DON'T follow the flip pattern:
- **ir** → **Vá!** (Go!) - NOT "Vai"
- **vir** → **Venha!** (Come!) - NOT "Vem"
- **fazer** → **Faça!** (Do/Make!)
- **ser** → **Seja!** (Be!)
- **ter** → **Tenha!** (Have!)
- **dar** → **Dê!** (Give!)
- **estar** → **Esteja!** (Be!)
- **pôr** → **Ponha!** (Put!)

Must memorize these!

**Negative Commands:**

Simply add **NÃO** before the imperative:
- **Não fale!** (Don't speak!)
- **Não coma!** (Don't eat!)
- **Não venha!** (Don't come!)
- **Não vá!** (Don't go!)
- **Não faça isso!** (Don't do that!)

Same form for negative - just add não!

**Polite Commands:**

Add **POR FAVOR** to soften the command:
- **Fale mais devagar, por favor.** (Speak more slowly, please.)
- **Venha aqui, por favor.** (Come here, please.)
- **Abra a janela, por favor.** (Open the window, please.)

Or use conditional (more advanced):
- **Você poderia falar mais devagar?** (Could you speak more slowly?)

**Common Command Phrases:**
- Espere! (Wait!)
- Olhe! (Look!)
- Escute! (Listen!)
- Venha! (Come!)
- Vá! (Go!)
- Pare! (Stop!)
- Siga! (Follow! / Continue!)
- Entre! (Enter! / Come in!)
- Saia! (Leave! / Get out!)
- Sente-se! (Sit down!)
- Levante-se! (Stand up!)

**Commands with Reflexive Verbs:**

Attach the pronoun to the end with hyphen:
- sentar-se → **Sente-se!** (Sit down!)
- levantar-se → **Levante-se!** (Get up!)
- calar-se → **Cale-se!** (Be quiet!)

For negative, pronoun goes before verb:
- **Não se sente!** (Don't sit down!)
- **Não se levante!** (Don't get up!)

**Signs and Instructions:**

You'll see imperatives everywhere:
- **Empurre** (Push)
- **Puxe** (Pull)
- **Pare** (Stop)
- **Siga** (Go / Continue)
- **Não entre** (Don't enter)
- **Proibido fumar** (No smoking - literally "Prohibited to smoke")

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- All regular verbs from Units 1-2, 8-10, etc. → now in command form
- Unit 35: Reflexive pronouns → "Sente-se!" "Levante-se!"
- Unit 15: Negation → "Não fale!"
- Commands use vocabulary from all previous units

**Key Learning:**
- Imperative mood for commands and instructions
- Regular pattern: flip the vowel (-a↔e) from você present tense
- Common irregular imperatives: Vá, Venha, Faça, Seja
- Negative commands: Não + imperative
- Essential for instructions, directions, requests

**Why This Unit:**
- **FOUNDATIONAL:** Commands are essential grammar structure
- Natural progression: know verbs, now use them as commands
- Ultra-granular: focuses ONLY on imperative mood (você form)
- Practical: immediate use for giving/receiving instructions
- Grammar milestone: major mood not yet covered

---

### Unit 72: Demonstratives - This/That (Demonstrativos)

**New vocabulary:**
- **Demonstrative adjectives/pronouns:**
  - este/esta/estes/estas (this/these - near speaker)
  - esse/essa/esses/essas (that/those - near listener)
  - aquele/aquela/aqueles/aquelas (that/those - far from both)

- **Demonstrative pronouns (neuter):**
  - isto (this - abstract/general)
  - isso (that - abstract/general)
  - aquilo (that - abstract/general, far)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **Three-way distinction in Portuguese:**

  Portuguese has THREE demonstratives, not two like English!

  **ESTE (this) - near the speaker:**
  - **Este** livro (this book - in my hand)
  - Near me, the person speaking
  - Equivalent to "this" in English

  **ESSE (that) - near the listener:**
  - **Esse** livro (that book - in your hand)
  - Near you, the person listening
  - Equivalent to "that" in English (near)

  **AQUELE (that) - far from both:**
  - **Aquele** livro (that book - over there)
  - Far from both speaker and listener
  - Equivalent to "that over there" in English

- **Gender and number agreement:**

  Demonstratives MUST agree with the noun:

  **Masculine singular:**
  - este livro (this book)
  - esse carro (that car)
  - aquele homem (that man over there)

  **Feminine singular:**
  - esta casa (this house)
  - essa mulher (that woman)
  - aquela loja (that store over there)

  **Masculine plural:**
  - estes livros (these books)
  - esses carros (those cars)
  - aqueles homens (those men over there)

  **Feminine plural:**
  - estas casas (these houses)
  - essas mulheres (those women)
  - aquelas lojas (those stores over there)

- **Demonstrative pronouns (replacing nouns):**
  - Eu quero **este**. (I want this one.)
  - Eu prefiro **aquele**. (I prefer that one over there.)
  - **Estas** são minhas. (These are mine.)

- **Neuter demonstratives (for abstract things):**
  - **Isto** é importante. (This is important.)
  - **Isso** é verdade. (That is true.)
  - **Aquilo** é estranho. (That is strange.)
  - Use when NOT referring to specific noun

**Practice format:**
- Point to objects: "Este livro", "Esse carro", "Aquele prédio"
- Practice all gender/number combinations
- Use distance (near me, near you, over there)
- Replace nouns with pronouns: "Eu quero este"
- Use neuter for abstract: "Isto é bom"

**Student can now:**
- Use three-way demonstrative system correctly
- Choose este/esse/aquele based on distance
- Make demonstratives agree in gender and number
- Use demonstrative pronouns (este, aquele)
- Use neuter demonstratives (isto, isso, aquilo)

**Typical sentences:**
- Este livro é meu. (This book is mine - I have it)
- Esse livro é seu? (Is that book yours? - you have it)
- Aquele livro é caro. (That book is expensive - over there)
- Eu quero esta camisa. (I want this shirt.)
- Você gosta desses sapatos? (Do you like those shoes? - pointing to listener)
- Aquelas casas são grandes. (Those houses are big - over there)
- Isto é importante. (This is important.)

**Sample conversation:**
```
[In a store, looking at shirts]

A: Você gosta desta camisa?
   (Do you like this shirt? - speaker is holding it)
B: Qual? Essa que você está segurando?
   (Which one? That one you're holding? - near speaker)

A: Sim, esta aqui.
   (Yes, this one here.)
B: Eu prefiro aquela ali.
   (I prefer that one over there. - pointing to far shirt)

A: Aquela azul?
   (That blue one?)
B: Sim, aquela.
   (Yes, that one.)
```

**Common Mistakes to Avoid:**
- ❌ Using "ese" (Spanish) instead of "esse"
- ✅ "esse" (correct - Portuguese spelling)
- ❌ "este casa" (wrong gender)
- ✅ "esta casa" (correct - casa is feminine)
- ❌ Using only "este" and "aquele" (ignoring esse)
- ✅ Use all three: este, esse, aquele (Portuguese has 3!)
- ❌ "isto livro" (wrong - isto is only for abstract)
- ✅ "este livro" (correct - use este with nouns)

**The Three-Distance System:**

**ESTE/ESTA/ESTES/ESTAS (this/these):**
- **Location:** Near the SPEAKER
- **Gestures:** "this here", pointing to myself
- Examples:
  - Este é meu livro. (This is my book - I have it)
  - Esta casa é minha. (This house is mine - where I am)

**ESSE/ESSA/ESSES/ESSAS (that/those):**
- **Location:** Near the LISTENER
- **Gestures:** "that there", pointing to you
- Examples:
  - Esse é seu livro? (Is that your book? - you have it)
  - Essa casa é sua? (Is that house yours? - where you are)

**AQUELE/AQUELA/AQUELES/AQUELAS (that/those):**
- **Location:** Far from BOTH speaker and listener
- **Gestures:** "that over there", pointing away
- Examples:
  - Aquele é o livro dele. (That is his book - over there)
  - Aquela casa é cara. (That house is expensive - far away)

**Memory Aid:**
- **Este** = "e" = "eu" (I/me) = near ME
- **Esse** = near yoU (listener)
- **Aquele** = "ali" (over there) = FAR

**Gender/Number Agreement Chart:**

|  | Masc. Sing. | Fem. Sing. | Masc. Plural | Fem. Plural |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Near speaker | este | esta | estes | estas |
| Near listener | esse | essa | esses | essas |
| Far from both | aquele | aquela | aqueles | aquelas |

**Neuter Demonstratives (Abstract):**

Use these when referring to IDEAS, not specific nouns:

**ISTO (this - abstract, near speaker):**
- **Isto** é verdade. (This is true.)
- **Isto** é importante. (This is important.)
- What is "isto"? An idea, a situation, not a specific object

**ISSO (that - abstract, near listener or recent):**
- **Isso** é interessante. (That is interesting.)
- **Isso** é bom. (That is good.)
- Often refers to what someone just said

**AQUILO (that - abstract, far):**
- **Aquilo** é estranho. (That is strange.)
- **Aquilo** que você disse. (That which you said.)

**Using Demonstratives as Pronouns:**

You can use demonstratives WITHOUT a noun (as pronouns):
- Eu quero **este**. (I want this one.)
- Você prefere **esse**? (Do you prefer that one?)
- **Aquele** é melhor. (That one is better.)
- **Estas** são minhas. (These are mine.)

**Common Phrases:**
- este aqui (this one here)
- esse aí (that one there - near you)
- aquele ali/lá (that one over there)
- isto aqui (this here - abstract)
- isso aí (that's it / that there)

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- Unit 3: Articles → demonstratives also show gender/number
- Unit 6: Adjectives → demonstratives are adjectives when with nouns
- Unit 55-68: All nouns learned → now point to them specifically
- Unit 28: Possessives → "este livro" vs "meu livro"

**Key Learning:**
- Portuguese has THREE demonstratives (este, esse, aquele) not two!
- Este (near me), Esse (near you), Aquele (far from both)
- Must agree in gender and number with noun (4 forms each)
- Neuter forms (isto, isso, aquilo) for abstract concepts
- Essential for pointing, specifying, clarifying which one

**Why This Unit:**
- **FOUNDATIONAL:** Demonstratives are essential grammar
- Natural progression: can name nouns, now specify which one
- Ultra-granular: focuses ONLY on demonstrative system
- Practical: immediate use for shopping, pointing, specifying
- Grammar milestone: fills major gap in curriculum

---

### Unit 73: Furniture and Household Items (Móveis e Objetos da Casa)

**New vocabulary:**
- **Living room furniture:**
  - o sofá (sofa/couch)
  - a poltrona (armchair)
  - a mesa de centro (coffee table)
  - a estante (bookshelf)
  - a televisão (television)
  - o tapete (rug/carpet)

- **Bedroom furniture:**
  - a cama (bed)
  - o guarda-roupa (wardrobe/closet)
  - o travesseiro (pillow)
  - o cobertor (blanket)
  - o lençol (sheet)

- **Kitchen items:**
  - a geladeira (refrigerator)
  - o fogão (stove)
  - o micro-ondas (microwave)
  - a pia (sink)
  - a mesa (table)
  - a cadeira (chair)

- **Bathroom items:**
  - o chuveiro (shower)
  - a pia (sink)
  - o vaso sanitário (toilet)
  - o espelho (mirror)
  - a toalha (towel)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **TER (to have) with furniture:**
  - Na sala **tem** um sofá. (In the living room there is a sofa.)
  - Meu quarto **tem** uma cama grande. (My room has a big bed.)
  - Using TER for "there is/there are" in rooms

- **Prepositions with furniture:**
  - **em cima da** mesa (on top of the table)
  - **embaixo da** cama (under the bed)
  - **ao lado do** sofá (next to the sofa)
  - **na** estante (in/on the bookshelf)

- **Describing furniture:**
  - sofá grande (big sofa)
  - cama confortável (comfortable bed)
  - mesa pequena (small table)
  - Adjectives agree with furniture gender/number

**Practice format:**
- Name furniture with correct articles
- Describe rooms: "Na sala tem..."
- Use prepositions: "em cima da mesa"
- Describe furniture with adjectives
- Say what's in each room

**Student can now:**
- Name 24+ common furniture and household items
- Use TER to describe what's in rooms
- Describe where furniture is located
- Use adjectives with furniture
- Describe their home in detail

**Typical sentences:**
- Na sala tem um sofá. (In the living room there's a sofa.)
- Meu quarto tem uma cama grande. (My room has a big bed.)
- A geladeira está na cozinha. (The refrigerator is in the kitchen.)
- O livro está em cima da mesa. (The book is on top of the table.)
- Eu preciso de uma cadeira. (I need a chair.)
- O espelho está no banheiro. (The mirror is in the bathroom.)
- Meu sofá é muito confortável. (My sofa is very comfortable.)

**Sample conversation:**
```
A: Como é sua sala?
   (What's your living room like?)
B: É grande! Tem um sofá, duas poltronas, e uma estante.
   (It's big! It has a sofa, two armchairs, and a bookshelf.)

A: E tem televisão?
   (And does it have a TV?)
B: Sim, a TV está na parede.
   (Yes, the TV is on the wall.)

A: Você tem tapete?
   (Do you have a rug?)
B: Sim, um tapete grande no meio da sala.
   (Yes, a big rug in the middle of the living room.)
```

**Common Mistakes to Avoid:**
- ❌ "a sofá" (wrong gender)
- ✅ "o sofá" (correct - masculine)
- ❌ "o cama" (wrong gender)
- ✅ "a cama" (correct - feminine)
- ❌ "Na sala está um sofá" (awkward with furniture listing)
- ✅ "Na sala tem um sofá" (correct - using TER)
- ❌ "em cima mesa" (missing "da")
- ✅ "em cima da mesa" (correct - compound preposition)

**Furniture Gender:**

**Masculine furniture:**
- o sofá (sofa)
- o tapete (rug)
- o guarda-roupa (wardrobe)
- o travesseiro (pillow)
- o cobertor (blanket)
- o fogão (stove)
- o micro-ondas (microwave)
- o chuveiro (shower)
- o espelho (mirror)

**Feminine furniture:**
- a cama (bed)
- a mesa (table)
- a cadeira (chair)
- a poltrona (armchair)
- a estante (bookshelf)
- a geladeira (refrigerator)
- a pia (sink)
- a toalha (towel)
- a televisão (television)

**TER vs ESTAR with Furniture:**

**Use TER for:**
- Describing what's IN a room (existence):
  - Na sala **tem** um sofá. (In the living room there is a sofa.)
  - Meu quarto **tem** duas camas. (My room has two beds.)

**Use ESTAR for:**
- Describing WHERE something is located:
  - O sofá **está** na sala. (The sofa is in the living room.)
  - A mesa **está** no centro. (The table is in the center.)

**Describing Rooms:**

**Living room (sala):**
- sofá (sofa)
- poltrona (armchair)
- mesa de centro (coffee table)
- estante (bookshelf)
- televisão (TV)
- tapete (rug)

**Bedroom (quarto):**
- cama (bed)
- guarda-roupa (wardrobe)
- travesseiro (pillow)
- cobertor (blanket)
- lençol (sheet)

**Kitchen (cozinha):**
- geladeira (refrigerator)
- fogão (stove)
- micro-ondas (microwave)
- pia (sink)
- mesa (table)
- cadeira (chair)

**Bathroom (banheiro):**
- chuveiro (shower)
- pia (sink)
- vaso sanitário (toilet)
- espelho (mirror)
- toalha (towel)

**Adjectives with Furniture:**

Common adjectives (must agree in gender/number):
- grande (big)
- pequeno/pequena (small)
- confortável (comfortable)
- novo/nova (new)
- velho/velha (old)
- bonito/bonita (beautiful)
- limpo/limpa (clean)
- sujo/suja (dirty)

Examples:
- sofá confortável (comfortable sofa)
- cama grande (big bed)
- mesa pequena (small table)
- cadeira nova (new chair)

**Location Expressions with Furniture:**
- em cima da mesa (on top of the table)
- embaixo da cama (under the bed)
- ao lado do sofá (next to the sofa)
- atrás da porta (behind the door)
- na frente da TV (in front of the TV)
- dentro do guarda-roupa (inside the wardrobe)

**Brazilian Home Context:**
- **Guarda-roupa:** Most Brazilian bedrooms have wardrobes (not built-in closets)
- **Pia:** Means "sink" in both kitchen and bathroom
- **Tanque:** Outdoor/service area sink (for washing clothes)
- **Área de serviço:** Service area (laundry area, common in Brazilian homes)

**Buying Furniture:**
- Quanto custa o sofá? (How much does the sofa cost?)
- Eu preciso de uma cama nova. (I need a new bed.)
- Onde posso comprar móveis? (Where can I buy furniture?)
- Tem desconto? (Is there a discount?)

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- Unit 60: House rooms → now filling rooms with furniture
- Unit 59: Prepositions → "em cima da mesa", "ao lado do sofá"
- Unit 16: TER → "Meu quarto tem uma cama"
- Unit 6: Adjectives → "sofá confortável", "cama grande"
- Unit 54: Colors → "sofá azul", "mesa branca"

**Key Learning:**
- 24+ furniture and household items vocabulary
- Correct gender for each piece of furniture
- TER for describing what's in rooms ("Na sala tem...")
- ESTAR for describing where furniture is located
- Essential for describing homes, shopping, moving

**Why This Unit:**
- **FOUNDATIONAL:** Furniture vocabulary completes house description
- Natural progression: have rooms (Unit 61), now fill them
- Ultra-granular: focuses ONLY on furniture and household items
- Practical: immediate use for describing home, shopping, moving
- Enriches ability to describe living spaces

---

### Unit 74: Nature and Animals (Natureza e Animais)

**New vocabulary:**
- **Common animals:**
  - o cachorro (dog)
  - o gato (cat)
  - o pássaro (bird)
  - o peixe (fish)
  - o cavalo (horse)
  - a vaca (cow)
  - o porco (pig)
  - a galinha (chicken)
  - o coelho (rabbit)
  - o rato (rat/mouse)

- **Nature vocabulary:**
  - a árvore (tree)
  - a flor (flower)
  - a planta (plant)
  - a grama (grass)
  - a montanha (mountain)
  - o rio (river)
  - o lago (lake)
  - o mar (sea)
  - a praia (beach)
  - a floresta (forest)
  - o céu (sky)
  - o sol (sun)
  - a lua (moon)
  - a estrela (star)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **TER (to have) with pets:**
  - Eu **tenho** um cachorro. (I have a dog.)
  - Você **tem** animais? (Do you have animals/pets?)
  - Structure: TER + animal

- **Animals with gender variations:**
  - **o cachorro / a cachorra** (male dog / female dog)
  - **o gato / a gata** (male cat / female cat)
  - But often use masculine for generic: "Eu tenho um cachorro" (I have a dog - could be male or female)

- **Nature with prepositions:**
  - **na** praia (at/on the beach)
  - **no** rio (in the river)
  - **na** montanha (in/on the mountain)
  - **na** floresta (in the forest)

- **Describing animals:**
  - cachorro grande (big dog)
  - gato preto (black cat)
  - pássaro pequeno (small bird)
  - Adjectives agree with animal gender

**Practice format:**
- Name animals with correct articles
- Practice "Eu tenho..." with pets
- Describe nature: "Na floresta tem árvores"
- Use adjectives with animals: "cachorro grande"
- Describe outdoor locations

**Student can now:**
- Name 10+ common animals
- Name 14+ nature vocabulary items
- Talk about pets using TER
- Describe natural environments
- Use nature vocabulary with prepositions

**Typical sentences:**
- Eu tenho um cachorro. (I have a dog.)
- Meu gato é preto. (My cat is black.)
- O pássaro está na árvore. (The bird is in the tree.)
- Eu gosto de ir à praia. (I like to go to the beach.)
- A montanha é alta. (The mountain is tall.)
- Tem muitas flores no jardim. (There are many flowers in the garden.)
- O rio é grande. (The river is big.)

**Sample conversation:**
```
A: Você tem animais?
   (Do you have animals/pets?)
B: Sim, tenho um cachorro e um gato.
   (Yes, I have a dog and a cat.)

A: Como são eles?
   (What are they like?)
B: Meu cachorro é grande e meu gato é pequeno.
   (My dog is big and my cat is small.)

A: Você gosta de natureza?
   (Do you like nature?)
B: Sim! Eu gosto de ir à praia e à montanha.
   (Yes! I like to go to the beach and the mountain.)

A: Qual você prefere?
   (Which do you prefer?)
B: A praia! Eu amo o mar.
   (The beach! I love the sea.)
```

**Common Mistakes to Avoid:**
- ❌ "a cachorro" (wrong gender)
- ✅ "o cachorro" (correct - masculine)
- ❌ "o flor" (wrong gender)
- ✅ "a flor" (correct - feminine)
- ❌ "Eu tenho cachorro preto" (missing article)
- ✅ "Eu tenho um cachorro preto" (correct)
- ❌ "no praia" (wrong contraction)
- ✅ "na praia" (correct - praia is feminine)

**Animal Gender Patterns:**

**Masculine animals:**
- o cachorro (dog)
- o gato (cat)
- o pássaro (bird)
- o peixe (fish)
- o cavalo (horse)
- o porco (pig)
- o coelho (rabbit)
- o rato (mouse/rat)

**Feminine animals:**
- a vaca (cow)
- a galinha (chicken)

**Animals with both forms:**
- o cachorro / a cachorra (dog - male/female)
- o gato / a gata (cat - male/female)
- o cavalo / a égua (horse / mare)

**Nature Vocabulary Gender:**

**Masculine:**
- o rio (river)
- o lago (lake)
- o mar (sea)
- o céu (sky)
- o sol (sun)

**Feminine:**
- a árvore (tree)
- a flor (flower)
- a planta (plant)
- a grama (grass)
- a montanha (mountain)
- a praia (beach)
- a floresta (forest)
- a lua (moon)
- a estrela (star)

**Talking About Pets:**

**Asking:**
- Você tem animais? (Do you have animals/pets?)
- Você tem cachorro? (Do you have a dog?)
- Quantos gatos você tem? (How many cats do you have?)

**Answering:**
- Eu tenho um cachorro. (I have a dog.)
- Eu não tenho animais. (I don't have animals.)
- Eu tenho dois gatos. (I have two cats.)

**Describing pets:**
- Meu cachorro é grande. (My dog is big.)
- Meu gato é branco. (My cat is white.)
- Ele é muito amigável. (He is very friendly.)

**Nature Locations:**

**At the beach (na praia):**
- o mar (sea)
- a areia (sand)
- as ondas (waves)
- o sol (sun)

**In the forest (na floresta):**
- as árvores (trees)
- as plantas (plants)
- os animais (animals)

**In the mountains (na montanha):**
- as montanhas (mountains)
- as árvores (trees)
- o céu (sky)

**At the river (no rio):**
- o rio (river)
- os peixes (fish)
- a água (water)

**Brazilian Nature Context:**
- **Amazônia:** Amazon rainforest (largest in world)
- **Pantanal:** World's largest wetland
- **Praia:** Brazil has 7,000+ km of coastline
- **Fauna:** Unique animals like tucano (toucan), onça (jaguar), capivara (capybara)

**Animal Sounds (for recognition):**
- O cachorro late. (The dog barks.)
- O gato mia. (The cat meows.)
- O pássaro canta. (The bird sings.)
- A vaca muge. (The cow moos.)

**Outdoor Activities:**
- ir à praia (go to the beach)
- nadar no rio (swim in the river)
- caminhar na montanha (hike in the mountain)
- acampar na floresta (camp in the forest)

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- Unit 16: TER → "Eu tenho um cachorro"
- Unit 54: Colors → "gato preto", "flor vermelha"
- Unit 53: Weather → connects to nature description
- Unit 59: Prepositions → "na praia", "no rio", "na montanha"
- Unit 66: Activities → "nadar no rio", "caminhar na floresta"

**Key Learning:**
- 10+ common animals vocabulary
- 14+ nature vocabulary items
- TER for talking about pets
- Nature prepositions: na praia, no rio, na montanha
- Essential for describing environment, pets, outdoor activities

**Why This Unit:**
- **FOUNDATIONAL:** Nature and animals are common conversation topics
- Natural progression: have locations, now describe natural environments
- Ultra-granular: focuses ONLY on nature and animals
- Practical: immediate use for describing pets, outdoor activities, travel
- Culturally relevant: Brazil has incredible biodiversity

### Unit 75: School and Education (Escola e Educação)

**New vocabulary:**
- **School subjects:**
  - a matemática (mathematics)
  - o português (Portuguese)
  - a história (history)
  - a geografia (geography)
  - as ciências (science)
  - a física (physics)
  - a química (chemistry)
  - a biologia (biology)
  - a literatura (literature)
  - o inglês (English)
  - a educação física (physical education)
  - a arte (art)

- **Classroom items:**
  - o quadro (board/blackboard)
  - o giz (chalk)
  - o caderno (notebook)
  - o livro (book)
  - a caneta (pen)
  - o lápis (pencil)
  - a borracha (eraser)
  - a mochila (backpack)
  - a mesa (desk/table)
  - a cadeira (chair)

- **School vocabulary:**
  - a escola (school)
  - a universidade (university)
  - a aula (class/lesson)
  - o professor / a professora (teacher)
  - o aluno / a aluna (student)
  - a prova (test/exam)
  - o dever de casa (homework)

**Grammar introduced:**
- **ESTUDAR (to study) + subject:**
  - Eu estudo **matemática**. (I study math.)
  - Ela estuda **português**. (She studies Portuguese.)
  - Use subject WITHOUT article after estudar

- **GOSTAR DE + subject:**
  - Eu gosto **de** matemática. (I like math.)
  - Ele gosta **de** história. (He likes history.)
  - Note: uses "de" as usual with gostar

- **TER aula (to have class):**
  - Eu tenho aula de português. (I have Portuguese class.)
  - Tenho aula às oito horas. (I have class at 8 o'clock.)

- **SER + adjective for subjects:**
  - Matemática é difícil. (Math is difficult.)
  - Português é fácil. (Portuguese is easy.)
  - Subject is singular even if "ciências" is plural

**Practice format:**
- Name school subjects
- Practice "Eu estudo..." with subjects
- Use "gostar de" with subjects
- Name classroom items with articles
- Describe school schedule

**Student can now:**
- Name 12+ school subjects
- Name 10+ classroom items
- Talk about what they study
- Express preferences about subjects
- Describe school and classroom

**Typical sentences:**
- Eu estudo matemática. (I study math.)
- Eu gosto de história. (I like history.)
- Tenho aula de português às nove. (I have Portuguese class at 9.)
- Matemática é difícil. (Math is difficult.)
- Eu preciso de um caderno. (I need a notebook.)
- O professor está no quadro. (The teacher is at the board.)
- Eu tenho muito dever de casa. (I have a lot of homework.)

**Sample conversation:**
```
A: O que você estuda?
   (What do you study?)
B: Eu estudo matemática, português, e história.
   (I study math, Portuguese, and history.)

A: Qual matéria você gosta mais?
   (Which subject do you like most?)
B: Eu gosto mais de história. É muito interessante!
   (I like history most. It's very interesting!)

A: E matemática?
   (And math?)
B: Matemática é difícil para mim.
   (Math is difficult for me.)

A: Você tem aula hoje?
   (Do you have class today?)
B: Sim, tenho aula de português às dez horas.
   (Yes, I have Portuguese class at 10 o'clock.)
```

**Common Mistakes to Avoid:**
- ❌ "Eu estudo a matemática" (wrong - no article)
- ✅ "Eu estudo matemática" (correct)
- ❌ "o giz" plural "os gizes" (uncommon error)
- ✅ "o giz" / "os gizes" (correct)
- ❌ "Eu gosto matemática" (missing "de")
- ✅ "Eu gosto de matemática" (correct)
- ❌ "Ciências são fácil" (wrong agreement)
- ✅ "Ciências é fácil" (correct - treat as singular)

**School Subjects - No Article:**

When using with ESTUDAR, no article:
- Eu estudo **matemática**. (NOT "a matemática")
- Eu estudo **português**. (NOT "o português")
- Eu estudo **história**. (NOT "a história")

But with other contexts, use article:
- **A** matemática é difícil. (Math is difficult.)
- Eu gosto d**a** história. (I like history.)

**Subject Gender:**

**Feminine subjects:**
- a matemática (math)
- a história (history)
- a geografia (geography)
- a física (physics)
- a química (chemistry)
- a biologia (biology)
- a literatura (literature)
- a arte (art)

**Masculine subjects:**
- o português (Portuguese)
- o inglês (English)

**Plural (treated as singular in agreement):**
- as ciências (science - plural form, singular verb)

**Classroom Items Gender:**

**Masculine:**
- o quadro (board)
- o giz (chalk)
- o caderno (notebook)
- o livro (book)
- o lápis (pencil)

**Feminine:**
- a caneta (pen)
- a borracha (eraser)
- a mochila (backpack)
- a mesa (desk)
- a cadeira (chair)

**Describing Subjects:**

**Difficulty:**
- fácil (easy)
- difícil (difficult/hard)
- complicado/complicada (complicated)

**Interest:**
- interessante (interesting)
- chato/chata (boring)
- divertido/divertida (fun)

**Importance:**
- importante (important)
- útil (useful)

Examples:
- Matemática é difícil. (Math is difficult.)
- História é interessante. (History is interesting.)
- Português é fácil. (Portuguese is easy.)
- Ciências é importante. (Science is important.)

**School Schedule:**
- Tenho aula às 8h. (I have class at 8.)
- Aula de matemática é segunda e quarta. (Math class is Monday and Wednesday.)
- Tenho aula de manhã. (I have class in the morning.)
- A aula começa às nove. (Class starts at nine.)

**Brazilian School System:**

**Levels:**
- **Educação infantil** (preschool) - ages 0-5
- **Ensino fundamental** (elementary/middle school) - ages 6-14 (9 years)
- **Ensino médio** (high school) - ages 15-17 (3 years)
- **Universidade** (university) - varies

**Terms:**
- **Bimestre** (2-month grading period) - common
- **Semestre** (semester) - also used
- **Ano letivo** (school year) - February to December

**School Supplies:**
- material escolar (school supplies)
- comprar material (buy supplies)
- lista de material (supply list)
- Common to buy supplies at beginning of year (January/February)

**Academic Expressions:**
- fazer uma prova (take a test)
- passar na prova (pass the test)
- tirar boa nota (get a good grade)
- fazer dever de casa (do homework)
- estudar para a prova (study for the test)

**University Terms:**
- a faculdade (college/university - informal)
- fazer faculdade (go to college)
- o curso (course/degree program)
- a matéria (subject/course)
- o vestibular (college entrance exam)
- o ENEM (national high school exam)

**Connecting to Previous Units:**
- Unit 69: Professions → professor, estudante
- Unit 48: Time → "Tenho aula às nove horas"
- Unit 25: Gostar de → "Eu gosto de história"
- Unit 49: Days → "Aula de matemática é segunda e quarta"
- Unit 61: Daily activities → "estudar" expanded

**Key Learning:**
- 12+ school subjects vocabulary
- 10+ classroom items
- ESTUDAR + subject (no article)
- GOSTAR DE + subject (with "de")
- Essential for academic conversation, describing studies

**Why This Unit:**
- **FOUNDATIONAL:** School is essential topic for students
- Natural progression: have professions (69), now education context
- Ultra-granular: focuses ONLY on school and education
- Practical: immediate use for describing studies, academic life
- Culturally relevant: introduces Brazilian school system

## Teaching Notes

**When do we introduce other pronouns?**
- você: Unit 23 ✓
- ele/ela: Unit 24 ✓
- nós: Unit 25 ✓
- vocês: Unit 26 ✓
- eles/elas: Unit 27 ✓
- **ALL PRONOUNS COMPLETE!**

**When do we introduce possessives?**
- meu/minha (my - singular): Unit 14 ✓
- meus/minhas (my - plural): Unit 31 ✓
- seu/sua + dele/dela (your/his/her): Unit 32 ✓
- nosso/nossa (our): Unit 33 ✓
- **COMPLETE POSSESSIVE SYSTEM!**

**When do we introduce tenses?**
- Present: Unit 1 ✓
- Future (vou + infinitive): Unit 29 ✓
- Past (preterite - regular -AR): Unit 34 ✓
- Past (preterite - regular -ER/-IR): Unit 35 ✓
- **ALL REGULAR VERBS IN PAST TENSE COMPLETE!**
- Past (preterite - essential irregulars: ser, ir, ter, estar): Unit 36 ✓
- Past (preterite - common irregulars: fazer, ver, dar): Unit 37 ✓
- Past (preterite - more common irregulars: poder, querer, saber): Unit 41 ✓
- Past (preterite - additional irregulars: trazer, dizer, vir, pôr): Unit 43 ✓
- **14 IRREGULAR PAST TENSE VERBS COMPLETE!**
- Imperfect (regular verbs): Unit 45 ✓
- Imperfect (irregular verbs: ser, ter, vir - ONLY 3!): Unit 46 ✓
- **COMPLETE PAST TENSE SYSTEM: Preterite + Imperfect!**

**When do we introduce pronouns (beyond subject pronouns)?**
- Reflexive pronouns (me, se, nos): Unit 39 ✓
- Direct object pronouns (me, te, o/a, nos, os/as): Unit 40 ✓
- Indirect object pronouns (lhe, lhes + review me/te/nos): Unit 44 ✓
- **Complete pronoun system: reflexive, direct, and indirect!**
- Combined pronouns (me lo, se lo, etc.): [Unit #] - Advanced topic

**When do we introduce other grammar concepts?**
- Negation (não + verb): Unit 18 ✓
- Comparatives (mais...que, menos...que, tão...quanto): Unit 47 ✓
- Irregular comparatives (melhor, pior, maior, menor): Unit 47 ✓
- Superlatives (o mais...): [Unit #]
- Conditional tense: [Unit #]
- Subjunctive mood: [Unit #]

**Critical decision points:**
- Do we teach ser/estar before regular verbs, or after?
- Do we teach articles (o/a) in Unit 1, or later?
- When do prepositions appear?

## Your Turn

Starting from Unit 1, what do you teach? Let's build this step by step.

**Guiding questions:**
1. What's the VERY FIRST thing you teach? (A word? A phrase? A sentence?)
2. What's the second thing?
3. When does "Eu sou brasileiro" appear relative to "Eu trabalho"?
4. Do students learn ser/estar first, or regular verbs first?
5. How many units/lessons before you introduce "você"?
